## concerts
- **Hammersmith Odeon (July 3rd, 1973) – Ziggy Stardust Retirement** : This infamous London concert, captured by documentary filmmaker DA Pennebaker, was David Bowie's "quits show." It marked the last show of the tour and the final performance of the Ziggy Stardust persona, concluding an extraordinary period in British rock. "The infamous Bowie quits show at the Hammersmith Odeon in London July 3rd 1973."
- **Station to Station Tour (1976)** : During this tour, David Bowie displayed his deep admiration for the German electronic band Kraftwerk by playing recordings and video projections of their album *Radio-Activity*. This demonstrated his interest in the Kraurock sound that would later influence his "Berlin Trilogy." "durante los conciertos del station to station. David Bowie ponía grabaciones y video proyecciones del radioactividad de Crabbro porque tenía una gran sesión con Crabbro."
- **Ziggy Stardust Debut (July 8, 1972)** : David Bowie debuted his Ziggy Stardust persona on stage at the Royal Festival Hall in London on July 8, 1972, introducing himself by saying, "Hi, I'm Ziggy." This marked the beginning of Ziggy Stardust's 360-day public lifespan. "That night, David Bowie stepped on stage at the Royal Festival Hall in London and introduced himself by saying, hi, I'm Ziggy."

## albums
**"Heroes" (1977)** : Released in 1977, this album is described as the best known of the three albums Bowie made while influenced by Krautrock during his time in Berlin. The title track is highlighted, and its B-side, "V-2 Schneider," was explicitly named after Kraftwerk's Florian Schneider, underscoring the direct inspiration. "The best known of those is probably heroes from 1977." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ePZDkqLM_gw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Heroes" (1977) - Berlin Trilogy Part 2, Masterpiece of Isolation** : The second album in Bowie's Berlin trilogy, arriving nine months after 'Low' in 1977, is best remembered for its title track, now considered one of Bowie's most cherished songs and called his "masterpiece." Though initially underrated and a modest performer (peaking at #35 on Billboard LPs), it depicted lovers by the Berlin Wall during the Cold War with innovative production by Tony Visconti, oscillating electronics by Brian Eno, and guitar drone by Robert Fripp. "Heroes has been called David Boey's masterpiece." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**25 Albums Recorded Before 1990** : 287 songs from David Bowie's 25 albums recorded before 1990 were used to create "Bowie Bonds." "287 songs from 25 albums recorded before 1990 became asset-backed securities." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pe40SqDrpZ0 ← david-bowie
**Aladdin Sane (1973)** : Released on April 13, 1973, this album was Bowie's first as a "genuine rock star." The "Aladdin Sane" character served as a transitional persona, evolving the "Ziggy Stardust" concept to a "higher realm" and being further developed through subsequent albums, even if not explicitly named Ziggy. "The Gene Genie written in part about his even crazier friend, Eiki Pop, and inspired by Jean Genie. Another friend who was a writer, poet, and political activist." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Aladdin Sane (1973) - First Album as Genuine Rock Star** : Released on April 13th, 1973, this was Bowie's first album as a "genuine rock star" and further developed the Ziggy persona into a "higher realm." The title itself, when separated as "A Lad Insane," hinted at Bowie's mental state and was influenced by his half-brother Terry's struggles with mental illness. "The next album, also called Aladdin Sane, was Bowie's first as a genuine rock star." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Aladdin Sane (1973) - Iconic Persona Evolution** : Released in 1973, this album further twisted Bowie's alien persona and made his look even more iconic, notably with its album cover featuring a bear-chested, flame-haired David with lightning bolt face makeup and a teardrop. Although its lead single "The Jean Genie" wasn't a big US pop hit, the potency of Bowie's persona ensured the album sold well, leaping into the top 20 and hitting number 17 by June 1973. "And they were joined by a new album that put a twist on Bowie's alien persona and made his look even more iconic, Aladdin's scene." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Aladdin Sane (Mid-1970s) - Character Name Origin** : Bowie's mid-1970s character was named "Aladdin Sane," a title that reflected his mental state during that period, punning on "A lad insane." "No wonder Bowie's mid-70s characters was named Aladdin Sane." ← Ongoing History of New Music > Alt Rocks Craziest People | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CgReNKciFJo&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Albums Released in 2010s** : David Bowie was among the "monsters of rock" from previous decades that came roaring back with new albums in the 2010s, contributing to rock's overall consumption and the health of the recorded music industry. "We saw albums from Pearl Jam and Soundgarden, Radio Head, Green Day, Allison Chains, ACDC, Metallica, Nine-inch Nails and David Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HSvgRyGiOpE ← david-bowie
**Berlin Trilogy** : This epic trilogy of albums was created with the significant help and collaboration of Brian Eno, who is credited for his contributions to its development. "ha creado su épica trilogía de Berlin" ← Por Qué Tu Cerebro Nunca Olvidará Este Sonido | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=86tqZ33gn_4
**Berlin Trilogy (Late 1970s) - Career Revival** : After a period of severe drug and alcohol abuse in Los Angeles, David Bowie moved to West Berlin in late May 1976 with Iggy Pop to regenerate. During this time, Bowie wrote and recorded three albums, known as the "Berlin trilogy," which adopted an electronic approach. These albums were instrumental in bringing his career back from the brink and became highly influential to a new generation of post-punk musicians. "It was during this time that Bowie wrote and recorded three albums that brought his career back from the brink." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AymMybE33zU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Black Star** : Bowie's final album, *Black Star*, is seen by some conspiracy theorists as confirming his "anointment" of Kanye West, who they refer to as a "Black Star." Theorists claim the album is "loaded with all kinds of coded messages." "What's the title of that last album? It's Black Star. And what is Kanye? A Black Star." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pmKjZzypzvg ← david-bowie
**Black Star (2016) - Last Legacy Album** : This album is musically, lyrically, and structurally complex, seen by Bowie as a final, independent legacy, distinct from his previous work. It incorporates influences from electronic jazz, rap, hip hop, drum and bass, and other electronic music. The recording process was complicated, involving many musicians including a New York jazz group, and only Tony Visconti was aware of Bowie's terminal illness during this period. The album achieved massive commercial success, becoming the best-selling vinyl album of 2016, more than doubling the sales of Adel's top-selling album from the previous year. "No tiene nada que ver con lo que había hecho de David Bowie anteriormente, musicalmente, liricamente, estructuralmente es algo complicadísimo y yo creo que él quería dejarnos algo completamente independiente de lo que había hecho como último legado." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Black Tie White Noise (1993) - Return to Form** : This album, released after Bowie had resolved his legal issues with a former manager and was free to make music on his own terms, was generally acknowledged as his best work since "Scary Monsters" thirteen years earlier. Despite its critical reception, it did not produce any hit singles. "In 1993, a record called Black Tie White Noise didn't result in any hit singles, but it was generally acknowledged to be his best works in Scary Monsters 13 years earlier." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Blackstar (2016)** : This album was released on Friday, January 14, 2016, just two days before Bowie's death. It is an excellent record that contains numerous lyrical and thematic references to mortality and his impending death. "His last album, Blackstar, came out on Friday, January 14th, 2016, two days before he died." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM ← david-bowie
**Blackstar (2016) - Final Album** : This album, Bowie's last, was also recorded in secret, with sessions beginning around July 2014, concurrent with his liver cancer diagnosis. Released on his 69th birthday, January 8, 2016, the album and its accompanying video are believed to contain messages left by Bowie about his impending death. "Once that was done, he started on a new record, also in secret, and it would be his last." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hhii2_BVE7A ← david-bowie
**Blackstar (2016) - Final Recording & Epitaph** : This album, released in the week ending January 30th, 2016, was David Bowie's final recording and his first and last number one album, reaching the top spot on the Billboard 200 album chart. It was described as an act of self-sacrificing genius, a combination of calculation, happenstance, inspiration, and fluke, serving as Bowie's self-written epitaph. "The week ending January 30th, 2016, when Blackstar, David Bowie's final recording, reached number one on the Billboard 200 album chart." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Blackstar (2016) - Inspired by *To Pimp a Butterfly*** : David Bowie's final album, *Blackstar*, drew its principal inspiration from Kendrick Lamar's *To Pimp a Butterfly*. Bowie explicitly stated his desire to create music that was complex, mixed styles, broke molds, and was written intimately, directly referencing Lamar's album. He listened to *To Pimp a Butterfly* continuously throughout the recording sessions for *Blackstar*, creating significant parallels between the two works. "Tutpim a Butterfly es la principal inspiración para el Black Star el último trabajo que hizo David Bowie." ← Music Radar Clan > Kendrick Lamar：  To pimp a butterfly | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ENmSJbhbGeo&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Blackstar (2016) – Easter Eggs** : The album's cover features a large Blackstar on a white background, with a star cut into five pieces below it that spell out "Bowie" upon close inspection. Exposing the vinyl to light produces a star-like reflection, or possibly a bird, while exposing the cover to sunlight causes the star to fade, revealing a starry sky; under black light, it shines like a star at night. The CD reportedly smells like black licorice when first opened. One font used on the back sleeve is called "Terminal" and belongs to a design suite named "Lazarus." The gatefold liner reveals Bowie's image on the right reflected eerily onto a star field on the left, where connecting the biggest stars forms a stick figure, reminiscent of Starman. "There are other things lurking, just waiting to be found." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Blackstar (2016) – Farewell Album** : This album, Bowie's final studio recording, was heavy on themes of mortality and death, and retrospectively seen as his farewell and a parting gift to fans. It incorporated elements of art rock, jazz, and various experimental approaches. Announced in November 2015, it was released on his 69th birthday, January 8, 2016, three months after he learned his cancer was terminal. Following his death, it sold incredibly well, becoming his only album to reach number one on the Billboard 200. "Blackstar became his only album to ever reach number one on the Billboard 200." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Chart Success of Albums and Singles (1972-1973)** : Between July 1972 and the end of 1973, all of David Bowie's albums and singles accumulated a total of 182 weeks on the album charts, demonstrating the significant musical impact of his Ziggy Stardust era. "If you add everything up, just to the end of 1973, all the albums and singles Bowie records spent 182 weeks on the album charts." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**David Bowie (1967) - Deram Debut** : This self-titled debut LP was released by the Deram label in 1967, but it ultimately failed to make the charts. It was issued after Bowie had found his name and voice but before he had found his distinctive sound or image, leading to him being dropped by the label in 1968. "Neither the single nor the self-titled David Bowie album made the charts." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**David Bowie (1969) - Space Oddity Album** : This self-titled album, released in 1969, was Bowie's second, although marketed as if his flop 1967 LP had never happened. It was rushed by Mercury Records to capitalize on the Apollo 11 moon landing. Later, RCA repackaged this LP as 'Space Oddity, the album', adding a newer Ziggy-era photo on the cover, which helped it break into the top 20 on the album chart in 1973. "After Bowie signed to Major Label Mercury Records, they rushed release the single to capitalize on that summer's excitement over the Apollo 11 moon landing, as well as a second self-titled David Bowie album, as if his flop 1967 LP had never happened." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**David Live (1974)** : A double-live album recorded in October 1974, capturing performances from the ambitious "Diamond Dogs" tour. This release contributed to Bowie's incredible output of five studio albums and one live record within a span of just two years and ten months. "That fall, October 1974, a double-live album was taken from the tour that made for five studio albums and one live record in just two years and ten months." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**David Live (1974) - Double Live Album** : This double live album was recorded in October 1974, capturing performances from the ambitious Diamond Dogs tour. Its release meant Bowie had put out five studio albums and one live record in just two years and ten months. "That fall, October 1974, a double live album was taken from the tour that made for five studio albums and one live record in just two years and ten months." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**David Live (1974) - Soulman Persona** : Released in 1974, this concert album showcased Bowie's R&B allusions, cracking the Billboard Top 10. Both the album cover photo, depicting Bowie in a silky suit, and the live arrangements, with songs like "Rock and Roll Suicide" rearranged to sound like Otis Redding, presented Bowie fully in his "Soulman" persona, crooning like an R&B artist. "These R&B allusions persisted on Boey's other major LP release of 1974, the concert album David Live. It too cracked the Billboard Top 10, and from the photo on the album cover to the live arrangements, Boey was giving Soulman, a screening in a silky suit and vocalizing like an R&B crooner." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Diamond Dogs (1974)** : This was Bowie's fifth studio album released in a period of just two years and four months, showcasing his remarkable prolificness. The album was loosely based on George Orwell's dystopian novel "1984," an ambitious and unusual concept for rock music at the time, which Bowie successfully executed. "Right an album loosely based on George Orwell's novel 1984? Try, nobody did that kind of thing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Diamond Dogs (1974) - Glam Rock Peak & R&B Hints** : This 1974 studio album broke into the top 10 on the Billboard album chart in under a month, peaking at number 5 that summer, cementing Bowie as a leading light of British glam rock in America. Despite the glam styling on the cover, critics noticed R&B allusions in tracks like "1984," hinting at his future musical direction. "Boey had amassed enough notoriety that his 74 studio album, Diamond Dogs, broke into the top 10 on the Billboard album chart in under a month, peaking at number 5 that summer." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Diamond Dogs (1974) - Orwellian Concept Album** : Bowie's fifth album in just two years and four months, "Diamond Dogs" was loosely based on George Orwell's novel "1984," demonstrating Bowie's ambitious and unconventional approach to album themes. This prolific period of album releases, each distinct and event-like, greatly contributed to his rise to stardom. "Write an album loosely based on George Orwell's novel 1984? Come on, nobody did that kind of thing, but Bowie did and he pulled it off." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Diamond Dogs (1974) – Unairbrushed Cover** : David Bowie's 1974 album, whose original cover featured a painting of Bowie with a Ziggy Stardust-like haircut, depicted as half-man, half-dog, complete with a "prominent set of dog junk." This artwork was deemed too outrageous by some, leading RCA, Bowie's label, to airbrush out the controversial detail on subsequent copies. An unknown number of original, unairbrushed copies were sold before the change, making them one of the most sought-after Bowie collectibles, with copies selling for up to $10,000 US. "The cover featured a painting of Bowie with a Ziggy Stardust like haircut. And Bowie is depicted as half-man, half-dog, complete with a prominent set of, uh, dog junk." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=tbmssCZ05ro ← david-bowie
**Early Albums (Late 1960s) - Acoustic Folk** : David Bowie's initial recordings were primarily acoustic folk, characterized by experimental and psychedelic elements. These early works recalled the sound of artists like Neil Young, Simon & Garfunkel, and Bob Dylan, embodying the late 1960s folk style. They achieved only moderate success, likely due to the market's saturation with folk music at the time. "Los primeros discos de David Bowie, aunque son muy interesantes, son principalmente discos acústicos de Folk, un tanto experimental, un tanto psicodélico." ← Music Radar Clan > EL PIONERO DEL GLAM： MARC BOLAN Y T REX | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Mw_HxfX8iBA&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Earthling (1997)** : This album garnered plenty of positive reviews and was supported by a successful "Love in the World tour." It featured the song "I'm Afraid of Americans," which included a Nine Inch Nails remix and a music video cameo by Trent Reznor. "Bowie and a 9-inch nails remix of I'm Afraid of Americans, originally from the 1997 album Earthling." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Earthling (1997) – 21st Studio Album** : Released in February 1997, about a month after his 50th birthday celebration at Madison Square Garden. Bowie was interested in new dance genres like industrial, techno, jungle, and drum and bass, incorporating them into the album. It sparked debate, with some calling it recycled, while others saw it as Bowie's official recognition of these genres, becoming a fine representation of his later work. "Honestly, Earthling is a good record." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Entire Catalog Released on CD (Year not specified)** : David Bowie was the first major artist to have his entire catalog released on Compact Disc. This marked a significant moment in the transition to the new digital format, making his complete body of work available to consumers in the CD era. "And the first major artist to have their entire catalog released on CD was David Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ak6OuOUkRrQ ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heathen (2002)** : This album marked a return to consistent musical output for Bowie in the early 2000s, suggesting he had no intention of stopping his recording career. "Meanwhile, Bowie continued to make records. There was heathen in 2002." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heathen (2002) – Return to Form** : Released in June 2002, this album marked Bowie's first collaboration with producer Tony Visconti since 1980, following a 20-year silence between them. It adopted a 70s-era art rock/art pop feel, incorporating dystopianism and dread reminiscent of albums like *Ziggy Stardust*, *Aladdin Sane*, *Diamond Dogs*, and *Station to Station*. The album was deeply affected by the 9/11 attacks, the birth of his daughter Alexandria, and the death of his beloved mother. Critics hailed it as his best work since *Scary Monsters* 22 years prior, reaching number 14 in the US (his best since 1984's *Tonight*), number 9 in Canada, and number 5 in the UK. "The whole thing was a welcome return to form." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977)** : Recorded in Berlin in 1977, this album features the title track which received special treatment from King Crimson guitarist Robert Fripp. Fripp was instructed to "do something weird," leading him to create three feedback loops using his guitar at different distances from the amplifier, which were then fed through an EMS synthesizer. The album also utilized piano, a special microphone setup, early synthesizers, and a Chamberlain keyboard. "Bowie was in Berlin working on what would become his hero's album, and the title track needed some special treatment." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) - Berlin Thematic Content** : Unlike "Low," "Heroes" is rich with continuous lyrical and thematic references to Germany and Berlin. These include allusions to the Berlin Wall, the divided city, the communist era, and the lack of freedom in the communist sector. This strong thematic connection to the city solidifies its reputation as the "heart of the Berlin Trilogy." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) - Berlin Trilogy Album** : The third album in David Bowie's Berlin trilogy was titled "Heroes." It was recorded at Hansa Studios, which was located within sight of the infamous Berlin Wall. The title track of the album was reportedly inspired by Bowie observing two strangers sharing a kiss by the Wall, adding a poignant, human element to the backdrop of Cold War division. "The third of Bowie's Berlin albums was called Heroes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AymMybE33zU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) - Berlin Trilogy Core** : Work on "Heroes" began almost immediately after "Low" was published in 1977. It is widely considered the true "Berlin album" of the trilogy, being the only one recorded entirely in Berlin. The recording process was very rapid, completed in just a few weeks, indicative of the strong working relationship between Bowie and Brian Eno, who had a clear vision. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) - Berlin Trilogy Part 2** : This album was one of the first two discs released by David Bowie as part of his "Berlin Trilogy." Its critical reception was significantly better than that of *Lodger*. "estuvo muy lejos de las críticas que había tenido con Giro, si que había tenido con Lodger." **Heroes (1977) - New Wave Precursor** : Recorded less than ten months after "Low" at Hansa Studio, this album continued Bowie's exploration of "crowd rock" and electronic sounds. Its title is a tribute to a song by the German band Neu!, and it includes "V2 Schneider," a nod to Florian Schneider of Kraftwerk. The record captured the nascent elements of what would become New Wave music, with Bowie once again ahead of trends. It is widely considered one of his all-time best records. "Heroes has gone down in history as one of Bowie's all time best records." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) - Optimism in Berlin** : Recorded at Hansa Studios, just 500 meters from the Berlin Wall, this album saw Bowie in a better mental state, aiming for a more optimistic vibe. It featured producer Tony Visconti, crucial collaboration from Brian Eno, and the same band from *Low*. Robert Fripp later joined, surprising Bowie and Visconti with his enthusiasm and adaptability, helping to define the album's epic atmosphere and creating unique sound textures. Visconti considered it a more positive version of *Low*, maintaining the structure of a conventional song side and an ambient/instrumental side. It was better received than its predecessor. "En esa época, Bowie se encontraba en un mejor estado mental, por lo que quería una hire más optimista para el disco." ← El proyecto que salvó a David Bowie. **Hunky Dory (1971) - RCA Debut & Commercial Potential** : This album, released in late 1971, marked Bowie's debut on the RCA label and showcased the first real evidence of his commercial potential. It won favor on US rock stations and cracked the Billboard album chart in early 1972, peaking at number 176. The album also featured tracks like "Oh! You Pretty Things" and "Queen Bitch" which played with queer iconography, complementing Bowie's emerging androgynous identity. "These songs, including Life on Mars and Changes, would appear on his late 1971 album, Hunky Dory. **Lager (1979)** : Released in the spring of 1979, this album reached number 20 on the Billboard album chart. It was mostly not recorded in Berlin, but rather tracked in Montrose, Switzerland, and New York City. The album employed the same Eno-centric recording techniques as "Low" and "Heroes," though it was characterized as less like Art Rock and more like quirky new wave pop. "Released in the spring of 1979, Lager reached number 20 on the Billboard album chart and spun off a couple of minor hit singles." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Let's Dance (1983)** : Recorded in just 17 days with a new session band, this album was a massive commercial success, selling over 6 million copies and becoming Bowie's best-selling album ever. The album, a hybrid of rock, dance, and funk, was groundbreaking for 1983 and led to the "Serious Moonlight Tour" which drew 2.6 million people across 16 countries. "Let's Dance was a massive success for Bowie, and drew 2.6 million people to the serious moonlight tour as it wound its way through 16 countries." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Let's Dance (1983) - Commercial Peak** : This album was conceived as a more commercially sounding record after Bowie's $17.5 million deal with EMI Records. Recorded with a new band of session players in just 17 days, including mixing, it was a massive and unexpected success, selling over six million copies and becoming Bowie's best-selling album of all time. Its hybrid rock dance funk sound was considered innovative for 1983. The album's success, however, caused Bowie to feel disconnected from his audience during the subsequent Serious Moonlight Tour. "Let's Dance was a massive success for Bowie and drew 2.6 million people to the serious Moonlight Tour as it wound through 16 countries." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Lodger (1979)** : Although the third album in Bowie's "Berlin trilogy," it was recorded in Switzerland and New York, yet maintained the stylistic feel of his German period with Brian Eno contributing (Tony Visconti produced). Initially the least commercially successful of the three and puzzling to critics and fans upon its spring 1979 release, it has since been re-evaluated as an underrated, artsy, and experimental album, anticipating new wave and post-punk music. "Lager was the least commercially successful of these three albums." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Lodger (1979) - Berlin Trilogy Conclusion** : This album, the third in Bowie's "Berlin trilogy," was not recorded in Berlin but in Switzerland and New York, though it retained the style and feel of his German experience. Brian Eno contributed significantly to its sound, helping Bowie explore his artistic direction, though Tony Visconti remained the producer. "Lodger" was the least commercially successful of the trilogy and initially puzzled critics, but it gained appreciation over time and is considered by Bowie officials to be perhaps his most underrated album. "It was called Lodger and it was the least commercially successful of these albums and critics really didn't know what to make of it at first." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Lodger (1979) - Berlin Trilogy Part 3** : Recorded starting in mid-1978, this album is described as the most complicated, controversial, and doubt-inducing of the Berlin Trilogy. It was not recorded in Berlin but in the United States, Switzerland, and some parts in Paris. Critical reception was mixed; it was often misunderstood, didn't receive excellent reviews, and was seen as the weakest of the trilogy upon release, with some critics not even considering it part of the trilogy. It features significant influences from World Music and Brian Eno, but fewer Krautrock and German music influences than previous albums, lacking their complex instrumental parts. Despite initial reception, *Lodger* gained significant charisma, followers, and fans over the years, becoming a point of inflection in the early 1990s as it contained the "germ" of much of Bowie's sound in the 1980s and 1990s. "Lodger que además, pues, es un disco complicado, es un disco complejo, a veces es un tanto polémico." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 3 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kU1JcEjezIc&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Lodger (1979) - Creative Shift** : Recorded in Switzerland with final touches in the United States, this album was created during a break in the *Heroes* tour. Robert Fripp was not involved; Adrian Belew (a future King Crimson member) took his place. Brian Eno's Oblique Strategies were crucial, inspiring ideas like playing old Bowie melodies backward and musicians swapping instruments to foster spontaneity. The album abandoned the electronic and ambient sound of *Low* and *Heroes* for more conventional songs, combining New Wave, World Music, pop, and Krautrock influences. While there were no arguments during recording, the creative spark between Bowie and Eno from their previous two albums seemed to be fading. "El disco abandonó el lado más electrónico y ambiental de sus dos anteleles trabajos a favor de canciones más convencionales, por decirlo de alguna manera." ← El proyecto que salvó a David Bowie. La trilogía de Berlín | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CHJwoQRxrKg

**Low (1977) - Credits Controversy** : The album's credits were minimal, with Bowie appearing almost in solo. Brian Eno was credited for some songs and production, but not as a composer for many of his contributions. This led to controversy, as many uncredited artists who were part of the creative and recording process claimed involvement. This lack of clear attribution was likely due to the dispersed recording across multiple locations over a long period, changing personnel, and Bowie's struggles with addiction at the time, making it difficult for him to track who participated. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Low (1977) - Critical and Commercial Success** : Despite Bowie's refusal to change the album and RCA's initial reservations, "Low" was released as he intended and achieved significant critical and commercial success. It was considered an "instant classic" upon release and performed surprisingly well in sales, exceeding expectations for its experimental and risky nature, although it did not reach the monumental chart positions of his previous "grand hits." Bowie himself was reportedly surprised by its success. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Low (1977) - Experimental Berlin Album** : Recorded at Hansa Studio in Berlin, this album was experimental and often very electronic, reflecting Bowie's fascination with German electronic music, specifically Kraftwerk. It was a colder-sounding record, made while Bowie was trying desperately to kick his cocaine addiction and experiencing physical and psychic pain. Side 1 featured short song fragments (none longer than 3.5 minutes), while Side 2 was entirely instrumental and included significant contributions from Brian Eno. Initially confusing to critics, it later became recognized as a bold work that expanded the reach of synthesizer music beyond its German origins, influencing post-punk bands like Joy Division. "Low, an experimental and often very electronic album that was part man who fell to earth, part station to station and part whatever was happening in Berlin at the time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Low (1977) - First Berlin Trilogy Album** : Recorded in 1976 and released in 1977, this was the initial album of Bowie's Berlin Trilogy, though most of its recording did not take place in Berlin, nor with "Dayan." The album came together from numerous unfinished or rejected projects, including outtakes from "Station to Station," an abandoned soundtrack for "The Man Who Fell to Earth," and material from "Honky Dory." Recording sessions occurred in Los Angeles, his personal studio in Geneva, and Paris, with Berlin primarily serving as a place for idea development. Musically, it incorporated influences from German Krautrock artists like Kraftwerk, Neu!, and Cluster, despite lacking direct lyrical references to Berlin. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Low (1977) - Release Challenges and RCA's Reluctance** : The album's release was delayed until 1977 due to problems Bowie encountered with both his current and former managers who still had financial interests. RCA initially refused to release the album, not considering it a guaranteed success despite Bowie's track record of producing chart-topping hits. The label suggested Bowie rework the album with more commercially appealing tracks. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Low (1977) - The Berlin Trilogy Begins** : This album, Bowie's 11th, was recorded at Château d'Hérouville with producer Tony Visconti and the core band of Carlos Alomar, George Murray, and Dennis Davis. Initially, Bowie was not entirely satisfied with the sound, leading him to invite Brian Eno to join the recording sessions. Bowie considered it a very special, melancholic album reflecting his mental recovery, thus believing it wouldn't be commercially successful. He refused to promote it, choosing instead to tour as a keyboardist for Iggy Pop, aiming to stay in the background. Despite initial mixed reviews, it performed quite well commercially. "En lausa respira melancolía, Bowie lo considera muy especial, grabado en una época de recuperación mental donde plasmoso estado, por lo que creía que no iba a funcionar comercialmente." ← El proyecto que salvó a David Bowie. **Peter and the Wolf (1969) - A Prokofiev Narration** : This album, a narration of Sergei Prokofiev's classical work for children, was recorded by David Bowie in 1976 during a turbulent period of his life marked by extreme drug addiction. The speaker claims the work itself was published in 1969 by RCA, who then decided to re-edit and release it with Bowie's narration. Despite featuring Bowie's name, the album did not sell well upon its release, being described as an "unbearable pain" by listeners. It was later re-released in the 1990s but again achieved low sales. This recording is considered a rare curiosity, often absent from Bowie's official or authorized biographies and discographies, existing outside of his conventional musical output. "el disco salió Pedro y el lomo narrado por David Bogud y con la fila de la fila de la fila de la fila no lo compró a mi perri porque después de la mente y sufrible tanto a la fila de la fila de la fila no porque es un coñazo insoportable y no por nadie." ← Music Radar Clan > Pedro y el lobo de David Bowie | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Hqx7Ev9NDJY&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Station to Station (1976) - Imperial Peak & Thin White Duke** : Anchored by the hit "Golden Years," this album, released in 1976, shot to number three on the Billboard LP's chart in just three weeks, holding the benchmark as Bowie's highest charting LP for the next four decades. **The Man Who Sold the World (1970)** : The original cover of this album, released in November 1970, featured Bowie reclining in a full-length blue dress he purchased from a boutique called Mr. Fish. This cover was poorly received in America, where many record stores refused to stock it, leading RCA Records to supply an alternative cover. Due to this controversy, the album sold only 1,395 copies in America between November 1970 and June 1971. "When Bowie released the album, The Man Who Sold the World, the original cover featured him reclining wearing this full-length blue dress." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**The Man Who Sold the World (1970) - Controversial Gown Cover** : This album featured Bowie on the cover wearing a flowing gown designed by British fashion maven Mr. Fish (Michael Fish). This look, displaying androgyny, was not encouraged in 1970, leading to certain stores in the US refusing to display the record and hurting sales until new editions with different covers were rushed out in places like the US and Germany. Inside the album, new songs indicated a significant creative opening for Bowie. "But Bowie didn't care, even as the controversy hurt sales." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

"Bowie had been well enough to secretly record an album and title the next day in 2013, something that took two years to make it a nearby studio that was within walking distance of his apartment." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hhii2_BVE7A ← david-bowie
**The Next Day (2013) - Secret Recording** : This album was secretly written and recorded over a period of two years, with no one involved leaking information. Its existence was announced on Bowie's 66th birthday, January 8th, 2013, along with a new song. The ability to record such an album in total secrecy during the internet age was considered a "miracle," attributed to the loyalty of his associates and Bowie's low-key life in New York. "The first the world heard of this record was on January 8th, 2013, Bowie 66th birthday. **The Next Day (2013) – Secret Comeback Album** : Recorded secretly between 2011 and 2012, featuring 29 brand new songs, this album was released on March 8, 2013, two months after the surprise single "Where Are We Now?". Its artwork was a cheeky takeoff of his 1977 *Heroes* album cover. It debuted at number one in the UK and number two in both the US and Canada. Critics considered it his best work since *Scary Monsters* (1980) and it was nominated for two Grammys, preceding Beyoncé as the first of a series of surprise albums released by superstar acts in the 2010s. **The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and The Spiders from Mars (1972) - Image-Making Breakthrough** : Bowie's fifth LP, landing in the spring of 1972, gradually became a sensation by early 1973, fueled by his new alter ego, the orange-haired glam rock alien Ziggy Stardust. This album proved to be Bowie's image-making breakthrough, cracking the UK top 10 and becoming his first album to break into the US Top 100 on the album chart, peaking at number 75 by early 1973. **The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and The Spiders from Mars (1972) – Alien Rock Star Narrative** : This album, released in 1972, was hugely influential and served as Bowie's commercial breakthrough, appealing to glam kids and future punk rock figures. It tells the story of an alien rock star named Ziggy, a name inspired by Bowie's friend Iggy Pop and Texas proto-psychobilly singer Norman O'Dan (The Legendary Stardust Cowboy). The music was originally intended for a full-on musical, stage show, or BBC TV program. The narrative describes a dying Earth five years in the future, with Ziggy initially ignored, then discovering "the Infinite's" (spacemen) who promise salvation, leading Ziggy to believe he is a prophet. Upon the Infinite's arrival, Ziggy dies on stage after contact due to their antimatter composition, after which the now-visible Infinite's absorb his essence. This album dramatically presented rock and roll theatrically with costumes, concept, and playacting, a style previously unseen. "The album tells the story of an alien rock star named Ziggy." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dm5N6yDRxXQ ← david-bowie
**The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and the Spiders from Mars (1972) - Persona Genesis** : The recording sessions for this seminal album were integral to the conception and development of David Bowie's Ziggy Stardust persona, including the creation of his iconic hairstyle. "The origins of Ziggy's hair is shrouded in legend. One version of the story says that during the sessions for what would become the Ziggy Stardust and the spiders from Mars album, Bowie woke up one morning and said to Angie over his orange juice, I want to cut my hair and I want to look different." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and the Spiders from Mars (1972) - Rock Opera** : This rock opera was released in the late spring of 1972 and details the story of Ziggy Stardust, an omnisexual rock star sent to Earth five years before its demise due to resource depletion. Ziggy is a messenger from the Starman, tasked with delivering a message of peace and love, but he is ultimately destroyed after believing too much in his own importance as a prophet. The album was added to the National Registry of the Library of Congress in 2016 for its historical and cultural significance. "Ziggy Stardust is an omnisexual rock star who is sent to Earth five years before it dies due to the people of Earth depleting its natural resources." ← For the Record - The 70s > Ep. 26 - Starmen - Glam Rock of the 70s | https://seventies.libsyn.com/026-glam-11820-6-34-pm

## songs
**"Heroes" (1977)** : This title track from Bowie's 1977 album is highlighted as the best known of his Krautrock-influenced Berlin period. The single's B-side, "V-2 Schneider," was famously named after Kraftwerk's Florian Schneider, directly acknowledging the German influence. "I'm going to play you the title track, but you should know that the B side of this single was called V Schneider, named after craftwork's Florian Schneider." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ePZDkqLM_gw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Heroes" (1977) - Cold War Anthem** : The title track of Bowie's 1977 album, "Heroes" is now one of his most cherished songs and considered a masterpiece, though it was underrated at the time (peaking at #24 in the UK, missing the US Hot 100). Its lyrics depict two lovers by the Berlin Wall during the Cold War. The recording features Brian Eno's oscillating electronic pulse, Robert Fripp's guitar drone, and Tony Visconti's innovative gated microphone system for Bowie's vocal, making it thunderous and anthemic. "Majestic, histrionic, soaring, ruminative, enigmatic, yet regal. Heroes has been called David Boey's masterpiece." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**1984 (1974) - Proto-R&B Experimentation** : A track from the 'Diamond Dogs' album, "1984" was part of a planned George Orwell stage musical that Bowie never fully executed. Critics noted its R&B sound, particularly its funky wah-wah guitar, which was compared to Isaac Hayes' "Theme from Shaft," and Bowie admitted its string arrangement emulated Barry White's Love Unlimited Orchestra, showcasing his proto-disco soul influences. "But critics noticed that deep on the LP's second side, the track 1984, part of a planned George Orwell stage musical, Boey never quite executed, sounded a lot like R&B." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**All the Young Dudes (1972)** : Written by David Bowie, this song was performed by Mott the Hoople and served as inspiration for Noel Gallagher when composing Oasis' "Don't Look Back In Anger." "His inspiration was the Bowie written, Moth the Hoopal performed hit, all the young dudes from 1972." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IhG-WJH9om8 ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Art Decade** : This instrumental track from the "Low" album is presented as an example of David Bowie's experimental music, particularly the instrumental side two of the record. "High two was not. It was all instrumental. And here's an example. This is called Art Decade." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pLf3kUONewg ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ashes to Ashes (1980)** : The music video for David Bowie's 1980 hit "Ashes to Ashes" prominently featured four members of the "Blitz kids" gang within the club. This inclusion demonstrated Bowie's appreciation and acknowledgment of the emerging fashion and style of this subculture. "David Bowie, with Ashes to Ashes, the video of which featured four members of the gang known as the Blitz kids." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mAlc-N2wn5s ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Be My Wife (1977)** : Appearing on the album 'Low' (1977), this track highlighted the album's use of post-punk guitars, electronic music, and Brian Eno's ambient sound. 'Low' was a departure from Bowie's previous pop sound, reflecting his experimental turn towards krautrock and electro influences during his Berlin period. "It bore a heavy influence from electronic music and Brian Eno's ambient sound, as well as post-punk guitars on tracks like Speed of Life and Be My Wife." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7

**Fame (1975)** : Co-written by David Bowie and John Lennon, this song originated from a conversation they had about the difficulties of being famous, with the lyrics co-written in about 20 minutes. It features Bowie's lead vocals and Lennon's background vocals (emphasizing "fame" in the verses). Although Bowie reportedly didn't like the song much and it was tacked onto the "Young Americans" album at the last minute, it was released as a single and became his first ever number one hit in America. "And it became Bowie's first ever number one in America." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Fame (1975) - First US Number One Hit** : Co-written in the studio by Bowie, John Lennon, and Carlos Alomar, this biting, spiteful song was a kiss-off to Bowie's former manager, Tony DeFries. Released as the second single from 'Young Americans' in summer 1975, it became David Bowie's first single to reach number one in America, also crossing over to number 23 on Billboard's Soul Singles Chart and being perceived as de facto disco on Top 40 radio. "Released as the second single from Young Americans in the summer of 75, Fame did something no David Boey single had ever done. It went all the way in America." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7

**Heroes (1977)** : The title track from David Bowie's 1977 album, recorded in Berlin, features notable contributions from King Crimson guitarist Robert Fripp. Fripp's part involved creating three distinct feedback loops from his guitar (an A note four feet from the amp, a G note three feet from the amp, and a similar third take) which were then processed through an EMS synthesizer. The song also incorporates piano, early synthesizers, a special microphone setup, and a Chamberlain keyboard, creating a rich texture with significant distortion and feedback. "Bowie with Robert Fripp contributing some distortion and feedback." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iGav9uJwA_w ← david-bowie
**Heroes (1977) – Multiple Inspirations** : This powerful title track from Bowie's 1977 album features artsy lyrics about two lovers finding optimism amid a world collapsing into death, including references to swimming with dolphins. Its meaning is layered, drawing inspiration from producer Tony Visconti's embrace with German singer Antonia Moss by the Berlin Wall, the Otto Mueller painting "Lovers Between Garden Walls," Alberto Denti di Pagano's 1956 short story "A Grave for a Dolphin," and a dream Bowie had about swimming with dolphins followed by a day with his girlfriend Claire Shenstone in East Berlin, watching soldiers. Bowie confirmed seeing Visconti and Moss, and Shenstone claimed their day directly inspired elements like dolphins, the wall, and gun shooting. "So which is true? All of them, apparently." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk ← david-bowie

**Sound and Vision (1977)** : Despite 'Low' not spawning major hits, this song was considered the album's catchiest track. It reached number 69 on the Hot 100, performing modestly on the charts. **Space Oddity (1969)** : This dark, pseudo-folk song was written by Bowie in the context of a painful breakup with Hermione Farthingdale, feelings of depression, and a fascination with the American space program, particularly the Apollo moon landing and the film *2001, A Space Odyssey*. The very first version was recorded on February 2nd, 1969, the day after his breakup. Several more versions followed, with the definitive one recorded on June 20th and released on July 11th, just in time for the Apollo 11 mission. Broadcasters, including the BBC, adopted it as an unofficial theme for the July 20th moon landing. The song became Bowie's breakthrough hit and turned him into a star, though he feared becoming a one-hit wonder. Its lyrics about Major Tom sparked speculation about the character's identity. Bowie recorded the definitive version after a chance meeting with Elton John led him to a producer. "The definitive version was recorded June 20th, and then released to the public on July 11th, just in time for the Apollo 11 mission." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie
**Space Oddity (1969/1973) - Major Tom's Journey** : Brainstormed after watching Stanley Kubrick's "2001: A Space Odyssey," this song tells the story of Major Tom, an isolated astronaut. It captured the 1969 zeitgeist, was rushed by Mercury Records for the Apollo 11 moon landing, and became a UK number five hit. In 1973, it belatedly became Bowie's first US Top 40 hit, peaking at number 15/16 on the Hot 100, years after its initial release. "He called the song Space Odyssey and it would change everything, ushering Bowie into his next phase." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Speed of Life (1977)** : A track from the 1977 album 'Low', this song featured post-punk guitars and bore a heavy influence from electronic music and Brian Eno's ambient sound. 'Low' was the first album in Bowie's Berlin trilogy, partly conceived from music originally intended for 'The Man Who Fell to Earth' soundtrack. "It bore a heavy influence from electronic music and Brian Eno's ambient sound, as well as post-punk guitars on tracks like Speed of Life and Be My Wife." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7

**Station to Station (1976) - Thin White Duke Introduction** : The title track of the 1976 album, its lyrics introduced the "Thin White Duke" character. **Suffragette City (1972)** : Originally released as the B-side to David Bowie's 1972 single "Starman" from the "Ziggy Stardust" album, "Suffragette City" later achieved greater recognition and is arguably considered a more significant hit within Bowie's discography. **Suffragette City (1972) - US Rock Airplay Staple** : A twin rocker from 'The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and The Spiders from Mars' album, "Suffragette City" became a staple on US rock radio airplay, along with the album's title track. This helped the album become Bowie's first to break into the Top 100 on the Billboard album chart in early 1973. "On US Radio, the album's title track and its twin rocker Suffragette City became rock-airplay stapes." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**TVC 15 (1976) - Cocaine-Fueled Fever Dream** : This song, featured on the 'Station to Station' album, was a number 64 hit and represented the album's lyrical themes of growing cocaine-fueled paranoia. The lyrics themselves described a fever dream about a girlfriend being eaten by a television set, reflecting the haze Bowie experienced during the mid-70s. "The TVC 15, for example, a number 64 hit was a fever dream about a girlfriend being eaten by a television set." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**TVC-15 (1976)** : Featured on "Station to Station," this song was inspired by a drug-induced hallucination or dream Bowie had with Iggy Pop, wherein an unidentified girlfriend was consumed by a holographic television, model TVC-15. It also reflected Bowie's immersion in the doomed spaceman character from "The Man Who Fell to Earth" and hinted at his future musical direction in the late 70s. "It was inspired by a dream, more likely a drug-induced hallucination with his friend, Ike Pop, where an unidentified girlfriend was eaten by a holographic television, model number, TVC-15." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Telling Lies (1996) – First Downloadable Song** : Released in September 1996, this song was Bowie's first offering available for download, with support from Virgin Records. It was revealed during an online chat where fans could interact in real-time. Three versions of the song were available, and despite a 7-megabyte file size requiring approximately 50 minutes to download on a fast dial-up connection, over 300,000 people downloaded it, exceeding all expectations for uptake. "The song is telling lies. It was revealed during an online chat, still a mind blowing thing back then." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**The Jean Genie (1973)** : This song from the "Aladdin Sane" album was written in part about his friend Iggy Pop and inspired by Jean Genet, a writer, poet, and political activist. The track captured the essence of Bowie's transitional "Aladdin Sane" persona, which took the Ziggy Stardust concept to a new level. "The Gene Genie written in part about his even crazier friend, Eiki Pop, and inspired by Jean Genie. Another friend who was a writer, poet, and political activist." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

**The Laughing Gnome (1967) - Kitschy Novelty Single** : Released by the Deram label in 1967, this kitschy novelty single, along with his self-titled debut LP, failed to make the charts. It represented a period where Bowie had found his name and voice but not yet his definitive sound or image. "That helped get Bowie signed to a solo contract with the DRAM label, where Bowie issued a self-titled 1967 debut LP, as well as a kitschy novelty single called No Kidding, The Laughing Known." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**The Laughing Gnome (1967) – Giant Flop, Then Embarrassing Hit in 1973** : Recorded on January 26, 1967, during a period when Bowie was struggling and desperate for any commercial breakthrough, this novelty song featuring cartoonish gnome voices was released as a single on April 14, 1967, and flopped entirely. After Bowie became a global star, old labels kept reissuing it. A 1973 reissue became a major UK hit — to Bowie's horror and enduring embarrassment. "An embarrassment for all time. **You've Got A Habit of Leaving (1965)** : Issued in the summer of 1965 by Davy Jones and The Lower Third, this was their debut single and was written by Jones himself. It was around this time that David Jones decided to change his name to David Bowie due to the rising fame of another British pop singer named Davy Jones. "Davy Jones and The Lower Third issued their debut single You've Got A Habit of Leaving, a song written by Jones himself in the summer of 1965." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Young Americans (1975)** : David Bowie began writing this song three days after Richard Nixon's resignation in August 1974, and it was released in 1975. The song is described not as an anti-Nixon track but rather as an observation on the state of post-Nixon America. It includes a direct question, "Do you remember your president Nixon? Do you remember you have bills to pay?", suggesting a contemplation on whether the public would remember the disgraced president or the circumstances of his departure. "He seems to be asking if anyone will eventually care that Nixon resigned in disgrace In other words will we ever remember how we got here?" ← For the Record - The 70s > Ep. 5 - Anti-Nixon Songs of the 70s | http://www.ftr70.com
**Young Americans (1975) - Stylistic Pivot to Plastic Soul** : The title track and lead single from Bowie's 1975 album, "Young Americans" was a seminal stylistic pivot, where Bowie fully embraced "Plastic Soul" and American R&B. It featured collaborators like Carlos Alomar and Luther Vandross, peaked at number 28 on the Hot 100 in the spring of 1975, and included a lyrical reference to The Beatles' "A Day in the Life" sung by the Vandross-led chorus. "Young Americans remains one of the great stylistic pivots by any artist in rock history. Boey fully committed to what he called Plastic Soul, going deep on his love of American R&B for the first time since the mid-60s." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Ziggy Stardust (1972)** : This song was part of the encore performed by David Bowie at the Hurricane Festival in Schleswig, Germany, on June 25, 2004. After completing this performance, Bowie collapsed backstage following his heart attack. "after a non-core that featured Ziggy Stardust, he made his way down the stairs of the stage and then collapsed." ← Ongoing History of New Music > People Who (Almost) Died | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7rXwaxlEkbQ&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

## curiosities
**"A Grave for a Dolphin" Story Connection** : The reference to swimming with dolphins in "Heroes" lyrics has a connection to a 1956 short story by Alberto Denti di Pagano, titled "A Grave for a Dolphin." This story told of an Italian soldier and a girl from Somalia involved in a doomed relationship during World War II. "Bowie remembered a short story written in 1956 by Alberto Denti di Pagano, entitled A Grave for a Dolphin." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk ← david-bowie
**"Ashes to Ashes" Music Video - £250,000 Cost** : The music video for "Ashes to Ashes" was exceptionally expensive for its time, costing £250,000. Made before MTV existed, its primary purpose was for distribution to TV shows like "Top of the Pops" to allow artists greater control over their public image, a major gamble for Bowie who had just emerged from a costly legal battle with a former manager. "The centerpiece of the record was ashes to ashes, a song that not only picked up the story of Major Tom from Space Audity, a character that Bowie had introduced ten years earlier, but it was also made into a hideously expensive music video that cost 250,000 pounds." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Blackstar" Recording Process at The Magic Shop** : Bowie recorded his final album, "Blackstar," in secrecy at The Magic Shop on Crosby Street in New York City, located just 283 steps from his Lafayette Street building. His daily routine involved starting work around 10 AM with a double macchiato from La Colombe coffee shop, and finishing by dinner to be home with his wife and daughter. "He started work around 10 o'clock each day with a double macchiato from a coffee shop called La Colomb. And he finished up at a decenar of the day so he could be home for dinner with his wife and daughter." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Bowie Quits" Concert (July 3, 1973)** : At the Hammersmith Odeon in London, Bowie staged a theatrical "retirement" for his Ziggy Stardust character, announcing that it was "the last show that we'll ever do." This event was captured by documentary filmmaker D.A. Pennebaker. Despite the dramatic announcement, Bowie did not actually quit, returning to the stage for a TV special less than two months later and continuing his recording and touring career. "Of all the shows on this tour, this particular show will remain with us the longest because not only is it the last show of the tour, but it's the last show that we'll ever do." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=huAvyInzz3Q ← david-bowie
**"Chameleon" & "Godfather of Change" Nicknames** : David Bowie was frequently called a "chameleon" and a "restless artist" for his constant reinvention and willingness to try anything for his art, switching between styles from glam to disco, synth-pop, and industrial rock. He was also known by other monikers such as "The Starman," "Aladdin Sane," "The Thin White Duke," and "The Godfather of Change." "They called David Bowie a chameleon, a restless artist who never stayed in one place very long, always changing to satisfy his muse." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**"Coming Out" Statement and LGBTQ+ Impact (1972)** : In January 1972, Bowie gave a "flippin' quote" to a British music paper, stating he had "always been gay." This statement, unthinkable for a celebrity at the time, given the legal context of homosexuality in Britain (decriminalized in England/Wales only in 1967, still illegal in Scotland/Northern Ireland for years, and military ban), became a bomb. Despite Bowie later recanting claims of being gay or bisexual, this declaration resonated with thousands who were afraid to come out, giving them courage. "This coming out struck a chord with thousands of people who wanted to do the same thing but were too afraid." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"I Want My MTV" Campaign** : David Bowie was one of the prominent artists who appeared in promos for the "I Want My MTV" campaign. This highly effective campaign encouraged people to call their local cable companies to demand that they carry the new channel, significantly expanding MTV's reach and power across the US. "Promos like this began to run constantly on MTV featuring the police, Pat Benatar, Pete Townsend, Cindy Loper, Billy Eidle, and even David Bowie." ← Ongoing History of New Music > The Rise and Fall and Future of the Music Video - Part 1 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lqd6IbUJ7tg&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Just David Bowie" Persona** : After nearly a decade of assuming distinct characters for each album, Bowie decided to present himself as "just David Bowie" for the "Let's Dance" album. Ironically, this decision itself represented a new persona that audiences had not seen before, shifting from a cult artist to a bigger-than-life rock star. "So after nearly a decade of assuming roles of different characters for each album, he decided to be just David Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"K. West" Sign** : The famous "K. West" sign, under which David Bowie posed for the *Ziggy Stardust and the Spiders from Mars* album cover on Heddon Street in London, was from a fur store. This sign has become a central piece of the conspiracy theory claiming Bowie predicted Kanye West's rise. It was later purchased by an anonymous collector with alleged music industry connections. "Forget that k West was a store that sold furs. It does matter, but if you sound the k West, you also get quest." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pmKjZzypzvg ← david-bowie
**"Leche y Cocaína" Diet** : During his profound period of drug addiction and decline, David Bowie was famously described as subsisting on a diet of "leche y cocaína" (milk and cocaine). This detail underscores the severe state of his physical and mental health. "De aquí viene esa famosa frase de que David Bowie se alimentaba a base del hechico caína, es justo esta época." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 1 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Irmc2d9KCM4&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Man Dress" Controversy (November 1970 - June 1971)** : David Bowie's decision to wear a full-length blue dress on the original cover of *The Man Who Sold the World* album in November 1970 was a highly controversial move in America. At the time, Bowie had little reputation in the US, and the country was not "ready for a feminized rocker." This led to record stores refusing to stock the album until RCA Records provided an alternative cover, and even an incident where a gun was pulled on Bowie in Texas. "America, not ready for a guy wearing a dress." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**"Retirement" of Ziggy Stardust** : At the end of the Ziggy Stardust tour, Bowie made a speech implying retirement, which many people mistook for his own. However, he actually meant that he was "killing off his Ziggy," already planning a new persona to channel his creative energies. "What he really meant though was that he was killing off his Ziggy." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**"Scary Monsters" Video (1980) - New Romantic Catalyst** : David Bowie co-directed a groundbreaking video for a song from his "Scary Monsters" album in 1980, which notably used the Quantel Paintbox for special effects. Shot at Beechie Head in East Sussex, the video was a dream sequence featuring Bowie as a clown, an astronaut (referencing Ziggy Stardust and the movie Alien), and a mental patient, with costuming inspired by "The Sound of Music." Extras from London's avant-garde Blitz Club, including Steve Strange (later of Visage), contributed to its distinctive look. Costing $65,000 ($250,000 today), this surreal and fashionable video helped launch the New Romantic movement of the early 1980s. "Bowie's surreal but very fashionable clown character helped jumpstart the whole new romantic movement of the early 1980s." ← Ongoing History of New Music > The Rise and Fall and Future of the Music Video - Part 1 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lqd6IbUJ7tg&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Soulman" Persona** : By 1974, Bowie began adopting a "Soulman" persona, evident in his concert album 'David Live', where he appeared in a silky suit and vocalized like an R&B crooner. This transition culminated in his "Plastic Soul" commitment on the 1975 'Young Americans' album, marking a deep dive into American R&B. "From the photo on the album cover to the live arrangements, Boey was giving Soulman, a screening in a silky suit and vocalizing like an R&B crooner." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**"The Man Who Fell to Earth" Role and Paranoia** : After filming the movie "The Man Who Fell to Earth," in which he portrayed a drugged-out, alcoholic alien, Bowie stole his alien costume clothes from the set. He then placed these clothes in a secure location, anticipating their use for when actual aliens arrived. "After filming the movie The Man Who Fell to Earth where Bowie played strangely enough, if he drugged out alcoholic alien, he stole all his alien clothes and put them someplace safe for when the real aliens came." ← Ongoing History of New Music > Alt Rocks Craziest People | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CgReNKciFJo&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**"Toy" Tracks on "Heathen" (2002) and B-Sides** : While the "Toy" album remains unreleased, several songs from the project appeared on David Bowie's 2002 album "Heathen." Additionally, a couple of other tracks from "Toy" were released as B-sides, with the remaining recordings reportedly stored in a vault somewhere. "Several songs appeared on a 2002 album entitled Heathen, and then there were a couple of B-sides, but the rest of the recordings are sitting in a vault somewhere." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gdWLtMy4TBU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**$17.5 Million EMI Record Deal - 1983** : In 1983, Bowie secured a monumental $17.5 million record deal with EMI Records, one of the largest in the industry at that time. In exchange, he committed to creating a more commercially accessible album. "And then there was the new 17.5 million dollar record deal with EMI Records, one of the biggest deals in the industry to that time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**1964 British Television and Newspaper Appearance for Long Hair Rights** : In 1964, under his birth name David Jones, Bowie appeared on British television and in newspapers alongside other members of the International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments to publicly defend the right of men to have long hair. "In 1964, Bowie, who was still known as David Jones at the time, appeared on British television and also in the newspapers with a few members of this association to defend the right of a man to have long hair." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**1964 TV Appearance - League for the Protection of Animal Filaments** : On November 12th, 1964, at the age of 17, David Jones appeared on television as a spokesman for a fictitious group called the "League for the Protection of Animal Filaments." This was a scam designed to get his friends on TV and earn about five pounds each, ostensibly supporting men with long hair. "He appeared as a spokesman for the league for the protection of animal filaments, a totally fictitious support group for men who chose to wear their hair long." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**1970s Visionary - Shifting Personas** : Throughout the entire decade of the 1970s, David Bowie was considered "a million miles ahead of everyone" due to his constant shifts in personas and images, and his relentless musical explorations across various genres. "For the entire decade of the 1970s, he was a million miles ahead of everyone with his shifting personas, his new images, and his musical explorations." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cy5SCQV0HAY ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**2004 On-Stage Heart Attack** : David Bowie suffered a heart attack on stage in 2004 while on his Reality Tour, during a period where he was reportedly happier than he had been in a long time. The initial signs appeared at a show in Prague on June 23, 2004, where he left the stage after nine songs, then returned, but performances were erratic, with "Station to Station" starting and stopping. "But he had a close brush with death on stage in 2004 when he suffered a heart attack." ← Ongoing History of New Music > People Who (Almost) Died | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7rXwaxlEkbQ&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**90s Reinvention - Sound and Vision Tour** : Bowie initiated his 90s reinvention with the "Sound and Vision Tour," a two-stage process beginning with a promise to perform his classic hits—such as "Space Oddity," "Ziggy Stardust," "Rebel Rebel," "Young Americans," "Heroes," and "Let's Dance"—one last time before permanently retiring them. His motivation was to clear away past expectations and start fresh. "The first was something called the Sound and Vision Tour, where Bowie promised to play his old hits one more time and then retire them forever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Acceptance as Performance** : David Bowie's onstage actions, such as kissing Lou Reed, were accepted by mainstream audiences because they were viewed as "theater" or "performance," rather than reflecting "real" personal identity or behavior. "dad just nodding and saying whatever when David Bowie kisses Lou Reed." ← For the Record - The 70s > Ep. 1 - Disco Doesn't Suck (Encore) | https://www.ftr70.com/blog/tag/70s+podcast
**Acting Career - "The Elephant Man" and Film Roles** : Bowie embarked on a significant acting career, notably performing 157 times as John Merrick in the stage production of "The Elephant Man," including a stint on Broadway. Throughout the 1980s, he appeared in films such as "Christine F," "Ball" (TV film), "Merry Christmas, Mr. Lawrence," "Yellow Beard," "The Hunger" (where he played a vampire, endearing him to goth fans), "Into the Night," "Labyrinth," "Absolute Beginners," and "The Last Temptation of Christ." "The acting thing would continue for the rest of the 80s. There was Christine F, a TV film called Ball, Merry Christmas, Mr. Lawrence, really good movie, Yellow Beard and The Hunger, all in 1983." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Acting Career - 1980s** : Bowie embarked on a significant acting career throughout the 1980s, taking on roles that were unusual for rock stars. His notable projects included John Merrick in the Broadway production of "The Elephant Man," films such as "Christine F" (1983), "Ball" (1983), "Merry Christmas Mr. Lawrence" (1983), "Yellowbeard" (1983), and a vampire role in "The Hunger" (1983) which resonated with Goth fans. He also starred in "Into the Night" (1985), "Labyrinth" (1985, for which he did the soundtrack), "Absolute Beginners" (1985), and "The Last Temptation of Christ" (1988), demonstrating a versatility unmatched by other artists like Elvis. "He had been in two movies at that time and was just embarking on his role as John Merrick in the stage production of The Elephant Man, which took him to Broadway." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Addiction Issues (Late 1970s)** : During the recording period of "Low" in the late 1970s, David Bowie was battling addiction problems. These issues contributed to the disorganized and dispersed nature of the recording process, making it difficult to properly track and credit all contributors. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Admiration and Collaboration with Arcade Fire** : David Bowie was a vocal admirer of Arcade Fire, praising their music and their self-unconscious artistic approach, which reminded him of his own early career in the late 1960s. He later contributed uncredited vocals to Arcade Fire's "Reflektor" single. "David Bowie have lavished praise on them." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ir2FfLQJNtY ← david-bowie
**Admiration and Rejection by Kraftwerk** : David Bowie was a great admirer of Kraftwerk, even playing recordings and video projections of their album *Radio-Activity* during his *Station to Station* concerts. He proposed a collaboration with Kraftwerk for his Berlin projects, but they rejected his offer, as they famously refused to work with anyone, including Kanye West. "aunque David Bowie siempre quiso que Crabbro fue una de esas mandas que la ayudó a grabar la trilogía de Berlin porque era un grandísimo admirador de Crabbro ... aunque se lo propuso y le espide por favor que grabas en con el Crabbro, nunca llevó acceder a trabajar con David Bowie." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 1 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Irmc2d9KCM4&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Admiration by British Punks** : The early British punks loved Bowie, admiring his concise songs, bold fashion, and rebellious attitude of not caring what others thought, even in the face of ridicule. His friendships with "cool" figures like Iggy Pop and Lou Reed, and his willingness to "kill himself off" creatively, also resonated deeply with them. "The kids who would become the first generation of British punks loved Bowie. They admired the short, sharp songs, his wild fashion sense, and the way he acted like he didn't care about what anybody thought." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
