**Advocacy for Pop Musicians with Long Hair** : David Bowie passionately articulated his activism for long hair, stating it was "for the protection of pop musicians and those who wear their hair long," acknowledging the "hell" that individuals with shoulder-length hair endured and urging unity. "It's really for the protection of pop musicians and those who wear their hair long, he said, anyone who has the courage to wear hair down to his shoulders has to go through hell." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Aladdin Sane Persona and Half-Brother's Struggles** : The "Aladdin Sane" persona (a play on "A Lad Insane") reflected Bowie's mental state, influenced by the struggles of his adored half-brother, Terry. Terry suffered from manic depression and schizophrenia, requiring hospitalization, and later tragically committed suicide by lying down in front of a train a little over a decade later. "Not only had the Ziggy experience been crazy for everybody involved, but he also had a half brother he adored named Terry, who was suffering terribly with mental issues." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Alien Abduction Paranoia (early-mid 1970s)** : Bowie developed a conviction in the early to mid-1970s that he was on the verge of being abducted and probed by aliens. To prepare, he carried a telescope everywhere to scan the skies, believing a mothership was coming for him. He also hired an assistant whose sole job was to procure every book on UFOs from bookstores. "Bowie became convinced that he was about to be abducted and probed by aliens." ← Ongoing History of New Music > Alt Rocks Craziest People | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CgReNKciFJo&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ambitious Diamond Dogs Tour (1974)** : The tour accompanying the "Diamond Dogs" album was one of the most ambitious rock had ever seen at the time. It featured elaborate sets, frequent costume changes, complex choreography, and a cherry picker boom that lifted Bowie over the audience during "Space Oddity." This hugely expensive and complex spectacle was groundbreaking, taking the basic rock and roll show to unprecedented levels of theater and spectacle, and audiences loved it. "The tour they came with the Diamond Dogs album was one of the most ambitious things Rock had ever seen." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

In an early 1972 interview with England's Melody Maker magazine, he came out as bisexual, instantly becoming an LGBTQ icon and glam rock's gender-bending avatar. **Androgynous Style and Gender Bending** : Building on his early 1960s long hair, Bowie embraced gender bending as a way to gain attention, notably wearing a flowing gown on the cover of "The Man Who Sold the World" in 1970 and in public. **Anisocoria (Eye Condition)** : David Bowie had anisocoria, a condition where one pupil was permanently dilated due to being punched in the eye by a childhood friend during a fight over a girl. This gave him an "otherworldly look" that contributed to his unique visual persona as Ziggy Stardust. "Bowie had something called anisocoria. One pupil was permanently dilated because he'd been punched in the eye by a childhood friend in a fight over a girl." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Antichrist Paranoia (early-mid 1970s)** : Around the early to mid-1970s, Bowie met two young individuals whom he suspected were trying to get him to impregnate them to give birth to the Antichrist. This led to extreme paranoia, causing him to be afraid of discarding anything personal; he kept his urine in the fridge and meticulously disposed of his toenail clippings. "Bowie met two young people whom he believed were trying to get him to impregnate them so they could give birth to the antichrist." ← Ongoing History of New Music > Alt Rocks Craziest People | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CgReNKciFJo&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Artistic Integrity vs. Commercial Pressure (1976)** : Faced with RCA's reluctance to release "Low" as he intended, Bowie refused to compromise his artistic vision by adding more commercial hits. The opposition from his label and managers ironically solidified his belief that he was heading in the right artistic direction, seeking to create music he loved rather than prioritizing assured commercial success. ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 2 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OpwDA0bUMw8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Artistic Philosophy - No Message** : In an interview with Cameron Crowe, Bowie stated he had "no message whatsoever" and "nothing to say," offering no suggestions or advice. He aimed to "suggest some ideas that will keep people listening a bit longer," hoping listeners would derive their own meaning and "come up with the message and save me the work." He accepted his role as an entertainer who did not take himself seriously, comfortable with personal interpretations from his audience, such as those by Jim Farber and other gay kids seeking representation. "I have no message whatsoever. I really have nothing to say, no suggestions or advice." ← For the Record - The 70s > Ep. 26 - Starmen - Glam Rock of the 70s | https://seventies.libsyn.com/026-glam-11820-6-34-pm

**Berlin Era Inspiration** : Bowie's profound admiration for Kraftwerk, combined with his love for German Expressionist art, was a key reason he chose Berlin as a refuge with Iggy Pop. This move was intended to escape the excesses of Los Angeles and to steer his artistic output in a new direction that aligned with the minimal and deeply German character of Kraftwerk's work. **Berlin Move and Addiction Recovery** : David Bowie relocated to Berlin specifically to overcome his addictions to alcohol, cocaine, and heroin. During this period of recovery, he collaborated with Brian Eno on three Kraftwerk-inspired albums, signaling a significant shift towards electronics-driven music in his career. "After moving to Berlin to kill off his addictions to alcohol, cocaine and heroin, he created three craftwork inspired albums with producer Brian Eno that show that maybe electronics were the way for." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iL9KpQFqH4o ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Berlin Regeneration and Routine (Late 1976)** : In West Berlin, David Bowie rented an apartment at 155 Hauptstrasse in the Schöneberg district, situated above a car repair shop. He established a routine that included having breakfast at a gay bar next door and exploring the city's unique areas by walking or biking. Following a heart attack scare in the fall of 1976, both Bowie and Iggy Pop began to earnestly clean up their lifestyles, leading to a period of intense creativity. "Apparently, Bowie also had a big thing for Hitler and spent a lot of his time touring World War II sites." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AymMybE33zU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Berlin Relocation for Detoxification** : Against all odds, David Bowie decided to move to West Berlin with Iggy Pop to detoxify and start a new life. He successfully and quickly detoxed, though he frequently entered and exited Berlin, never staying for more than six months consecutively due to ongoing legal processes in Paris, divorce proceedings, and other commitments. "es justo cuando, en contra todo pronóstico, el yipop deciden mudar Seppardin para desintoxicarse y empezar una nueva vida." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 1 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Irmc2d9KCM4&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Berlin Trilogy Production** : David Bowie's work in Berlin, specifically his production of his own records and those of Iggy Pop alongside Brian Eno, was a significant reference point for the avant-garde faction of punk and the nascent post-punk movement. **Birth & Early Life** : Born David Robert Jones in Brixton in 1947, and largely raised in the London borough of Bromley, he showed early ambition, telling his parents he intended to become a pop star. He began performing at age 13, learned the saxophone while at Bromley Technical High School, and formed his first band at 15. "The young man born David Robert Jones in Brixton in 1947. Largely raised in the London borough of Bromley, the ambitious Jones, who told his parents he intended to become a pop star, began performing at age 13, learned the saxophone while at Bromley Technical High School, and formed his first band at 15." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Bitter Split from Tony DeFries (April 1975)** : Following Bowie's decision to split from Tony DeFries, a 48-hour marathon negotiation took place in April 1975 to finalize his departure. The terms of the split were so harsh that it's said Bowie broke down and cried at the conference table, remaining in shock for a week. The agreement stipulated that Bowie could leave only if Main Man took half of his earnings from albums dating back to *Hunky Dory* in 1971 through an upcoming live album, and DeFries was guaranteed 16% of Bowie's gross earnings for the next seven years, through to 1982. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PzyvXmDKFUc ← david-bowie
**Black Star Posthumous Success and Initial Edition** : Black Star was released three days before David Bowie's death. The initial edition sold out almost instantly following his passing, leading to a period where the album was unavailable before a massive re-release. Copies from these first three or four days, available in transparent or black vinyl, are considered valuable collector's items. "una es los primeros días esos tres días que hubo entre el lanzamiento de la muerte de David Bowie, en el cual sale la primera edición del Black Star y la cual se agota casi instantáneamente tras su muerte." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Black Star Production Difficulties** : The production of Black Star was initially planned with three producers: David Bowie, Tony Visconti, and James Murphy. However, James Murphy, overwhelmed by other projects and unaware of Bowie's terminal illness, was often late or absent, didn't understand the material, and ultimately declined a full producer credit, contributing only specific rhythmic and sound elements. "Por desgracia la cosa salió muy mal." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Black Star as an Unheard Artwork** : Despite its massive sales, especially posthumously, many buyers of Black Star may not actively listen to the album because of its complex art-jazz nature. It's suggested that many purchased it out of affection or as a farewell to the artist, rather than for regular listening, perhaps only engaging with a song like "Lazarus." "Resulta un tanto triste que mucha gente se ha comprado y no lo vaya a escuchar operativamente, no le escucha, al final es un disco de Arjas muy complejo que contrasta mucho con las ventas masivas que tiene." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Blackstar Release on 69th Birthday (January 8, 2016)** : Bowie's final album, "Blackstar," was released on Friday, January 8, 2016, coinciding with his 69th birthday. That same night, Holy Holy, a band featuring some of his former Spiders from Mars backing musicians, played a show in New York City, and while there was speculation Bowie might appear, he did not; instead, the band left him a voicemail with the crowd singing "Happy Birthday." "On Friday, January 18, the day Blackstar, that album he'd been working on during his illness, was released, and it was also Bowie's 69th birthday." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hhii2_BVE7A ← david-bowie
**Blue-Eyed Plastic Soul Singer** : The "Young Americans" album introduced a new Bowie persona: the "blue-eyed plastic soul singer." This look featured a new haircut with a part on the right, baggy pants, and stylishly baggy sweatshirts, embodying a professed love for black music. This endorsement encouraged many of his fans to explore soul and R&B. "Young Americans introduced yet another Bowie. The blue-eyed plastic soul singer." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Bonds Downgraded Due to Internet Sales Decline** : Despite their innovative nature, Bowie Bonds were downgraded to junk status by 2004, approximately seven years after their creation. This downgrade was a direct consequence of declining music sales brought on by the rise of the internet, an irony given Bowie's own prophecy about music becoming "cheap as water" due to internet distribution. "By 2004, about seven years in, those bonds were downgraded to junk status. Why? Well, because of declining music sales brought on by the rise of the internet." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Bowie Bonds (1997) – Financial Innovation** : In 1997, Bowie, with banker David Pullman, pioneered "Bowie Bonds," a financial instrument where he securitized his future music royalties as collateral to issue bonds. He sold these bonds, raising $55 million, which he then used to repurchase the rights to his music that he had lost through previous bad management deals with Tony DeFries. This marked the first time a performer used their cash flow potential in this manner. Issued a few years before widespread music piracy, the bonds initially had a high A3 rating and paid 7.9% interest over 10 years, attracting Prudential Insurance. However, within 18 months, the music industry tanked due to Napster and declining physical sales, causing the bonds' rating to drop to BAA3 (near junk status). In 2007, the bonds were liquidated, and all music rights reverted to Bowie, meaning by his death in 2016, he owned almost everything he had produced. "This was the first time in financial history that a performer had used their cash flow potential to make money." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Bowie Bonds - Financial Innovation** : In 1997, Bowie collaborated with New York investment banker David Pullman to create "Bowie Bonds," a package of securities backed by the future projected royalties of 25 Bowie albums (287 songs recorded before 1990). Bowie received $55 million upfront, using the money to buy back rights he had lost to his former manager. This was a pioneering use of intellectual property to secure a financial instrument. "In 1997, a New York investment banker named David Pullman put together a package of securities backed by the future projected royalties of 25 Bowie albums, a total of 287 songs that were recorded before 1990." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Bowie Bonds Hit Junk Status (2007)** : By 2007, ten years after their inception, record sales had dropped so significantly, and royalties had dried up to such an extent, that the Bowie Bonds lost their value, hitting "junk status." "Bottom line was that after 10 years, record sales had dropped so much, and royalties on these sales had dried up so much that Bowie bonds hit junk status." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pe40SqDrpZ0 ← david-bowie
**Bowie Net (1997-2006) – Pioneering ISP** : Over a couple of years, Bowie and a small team created Bowie Net, launched around 1997-1998, which functioned as an internet service provider. Subscribers paid $20 a month for internet access and a @DavidBowie.com email address, or $6 for access to exclusive content like songs, music videos, chat rooms, images of his paintings, and journal writings. Bowie was known to lurk anonymously in chat rooms. In 1999, it held a song contest with 80,000 lyric submissions, won by Alex Grant whose lyrics appeared on the *Hours* album. It featured LiveAndWell.com for live tracks and Bowie World, a 3D virtual environment where users could navigate a Bowie-themed city as avatars and communicate with other fans. At its peak in 1999, Bowie Net had 100,000 customers but ceased operations in 2006 as larger companies copied his innovations. "Bowie Net was incredibly ahead of its time." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Bowie's Foresight on Internet Disruption** : At the time of the Bowie Bonds' creation, many considered his decision to forfeit royalties as "crazy." However, Bowie was studying the emerging internet and correctly predicted its disruptive impact on the music business, anticipating a decline in traditional record royalties, which materialized with the rise of Napster and file-sharing. "At the time, though, people thought that Bowie was crazy giving up his songs like this. But Bowie knew what was coming. He was studying this new thing called the Internet, and he knew that it was going to completely disrupt the music business, and he knew that old school record royalties were going to drop, which is exactly what happened, especially when Napster and all the other file-trading programs popped up." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pe40SqDrpZ0 ← david-bowie
**Bowie's Influence on Rock and Roll** : David Bowie, particularly through his Ziggy Stardust alter ego, profoundly altered the trajectory of rock and roll's development and served as a powerful source of inspiration for countless aspiring rock musicians globally. "How Bowie and Ziggy changed the course of the development of rock and roll." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Bowie's Listening Habits During Black Star Recording** : David Bowie had a compulsive listening habit during the recording of Black Star. He became a huge follower of Börtshoff Canadá in his final years and listened to their music almost compulsively. He was also deeply fascinated by the hip hop trio Dead Grips and considered Kendrick Lamar's album *Tu Pimp a Butterfly* an "authentic masterpiece," which he listened to continuously as a major influence. "él se convierte un grandísimo seguidor de Börtshoff Canadá en los últimos años y escuchaba Börtshoff Canadá de manera casi compulsiva durante la grabación del Black Star." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Bowie's Reaction to Lost Tape Story** : Years later, the speaker recounted the lost tape story to Bowie, who listened intently, placed his hands on the speaker's shoulders, and said, "well, that was stupid if he wasn't it." This was the last interaction they had. "And he's listening intently and he puts his hands on my shoulders and stares me in the eye and says, well, that was stupid if he wasn't it." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=4xxgPX-aR90 ← david-bowie
**Bowie-esque Style** : David Bowie is used as an example of an artist whose distinct approach to music inspires others, with artists often being described as "Bowie-esque" if their work conjures similar images. This illustrates the concept of artists building on the accomplishments of those who came before them. "How many times have you heard an artist describe this bowie-esque because their approach to music conjures images of what David Bowie did?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fS8V3kYXT6w ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

His influence was so strong that it was difficult to find a punk enthusiast in London who wasn't also a Bowie fan. He is considered one of the most important figures for gay people in pop culture, with tremendous social and political implications, especially in the UK. **Claire Shenstone's Day Out with Bowie** : During the recording of the *Heroes* album, Bowie spent a day with his then-girlfriend, model, and artist Claire Shenstone. The night before, Bowie had dreamt he was swimming with dolphins. The next day, they visited East Berlin and observed soldiers marching, an experience which Shenstone claims directly inspired the song's lyrics, specifically the references to dolphins, standing by the wall, and gunshots. "Shenstone claims that the song's lyrics were directly inspired by that day they spent together." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk ← david-bowie

**Cocaine Addiction and Paranoia in Los Angeles (1974-1976)** : Between 1974 and 1976, Bowie was deeply entrenched in cocaine and alcohol addiction, a state exacerbated by his move to Los Angeles, the "cocaine capital of North America." This led to severe cocaine-induced paranoia, a common reaction among users, with Bowie's focus on witches. "Between 1974 and sometime in 1976, Bowie was an absolute mess." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU ← david-bowie

This period heavily influenced his lyrics on the 'Station to Station' album, reflecting growing paranoia, and he later claimed not to remember anything about the album's creation due to his raging addiction. **Concerts as Theater** : With Ziggy Stardust, Bowie transformed rock concerts from mere performances by musicians standing on a low stage into theatrical spectacles. These shows incorporated choreography and elaborate costuming, making the concert an integral part of the "show" itself, blending hard rock with vaudeville, glitter pop with real theater, and fashion with technology. "Back then, concerts were basically a bunch of dude standing around on a low stage. But with Ziggy, the concert was theater, a spectacle with its choreography and costuming." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Confidence from "Space Oddity" Success** : The success of "Space Oddity," particularly its high chart position in the UK, provided Bowie with much-needed confidence. This newfound self-assurance encouraged him to be even bolder with his experiments in image and presentation, leading to his iconic gender-bending styles. "This success gave Bowie some much needed confidence. He felt he could even be more bold with his experiments with the image and presentation, which often involves some serious gender bending." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Consequence of "Man Dress" Failure** : The commercial and cultural failure of *The Man Who Sold the World*'s dress cover, which sold less than 1,400 copies in America in its first seven months, directly influenced Bowie's subsequent artistic direction. This setback prompted him to develop a more "palatable" character for American audiences, leading directly to the creation of Ziggy Stardust. "Bowie's gamble to wear a dress in public was such a failure that he immediately started thinking about how he could morph into something a little bit more palatable for American taste." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**Continued Support for Iggy Pop** : Despite their paths diverging after the Berlin Trilogy, David Bowie consistently provided support to Iggy Pop, most notably through royalties from his cover of "China Girl," which helped Iggy Pop financially. "el propio David Bowie nunca habría terminado de darle cierto apoyo a Iguipop en ese sentido." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie： La trilogía de Berlin 3 | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kU1JcEjezIc&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Contractual Dispute with Main Man (1972-1975)** : David Bowie wanted out of his contract with Tony DeFries' management company, Main Man, by the end of 1974, just two years into their relationship. Despite selling millions of albums, Bowie realized that most of the profits were not reaching him, suspecting that the new contract signed with Main Man at the end of September 1972 was "weird." On January 29, 1975, Bowie informed RCA, his record label, of his intention to split from DeFries, sparking a battle over who owned Bowie's next album. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PzyvXmDKFUc ← david-bowie
**Correct Pronunciation of "Bowie"** : The correct pronunciation of his adopted surname is "Bowie," not "Bowie" or "Bow-ee." Bowie himself affirmed this pronunciation, despite guitarist Mick Ronson and others sometimes mispronouncing it. "It should be pronounced Bowie. And trust me, I spoke to the man himself." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

**Creation of Bowie Bonds (1997)** : In 1997, David Bowie, in collaboration with investment banker David Pullman, created a financial instrument called "Bowie Bonds." This involved securitizing 287 songs from 25 albums recorded before 1990, effectively making them asset-backed securities. In exchange for forfeiting 10 years of royalty income, Bowie received an immediate lump sum payment of $55 million. He utilized this money to repurchase the rights to songs he had lost to his former manager, Tony DeFrees. "David Bowie and an investment banker named David Pullman created a financial instrument called Bowie Bonds. To use Wall Street speak, 287 songs from 25 albums recorded before 1990 became asset-backed securities. In exchange for forfeiting royalty income for a period of 10 years, Bowie received an immediate payment of $55 million. He used that money to buy out the rights to songs he lost to his former manager, Tony DeFrees." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pe40SqDrpZ0 ← david-bowie
**Creation of Ziggy Stardust** : Building on glam rock concepts, Bowie developed the character Ziggy Stardust. This persona was inspired by the outrageous behavior of Iggy Pop and The Stooges, the artsy "scummy" persona of Lou Reed and the Velvet Underground, the "god-alien" self-perception of Vince Taylor, and the "space travel obsessed" persona of Norman Odom, also known as the Legendary Stardust Cowboy. Bowie combined these influences, changing "Iggy" to "Ziggy" and adopting "Stardust" as the surname. "He invented an entire character completely rooted in glam rock concepts that borrowed from the outrageous behavior of another new friend, Iggy Pop... So Bowie, taking all this information, changed Iggy to Ziggy and adopted Stardust as a surname and thus Ziggy Stardust was born." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Cremation and Ashes in Bali** : Following his death on January 10th, 2016, Bowie's body was cremated. In his will, he requested that his ashes be scattered in Bali and stipulated that there should be no funeral. "His body was cremated, and he asked in his will that his ashes be scattered in Bali. He left instructions that there be no funeral." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Critical Decline in the 80s** : During the mid-to-late 1980s, Bowie's music and performances, including albums like "Tonight" and "Never Let Me Down," and the "Glass Spiders tour," faced harsh criticism, with descriptions like "tired" and "fake enthusiasm" being used to characterize his work, suggesting a departure from his earlier innovative spirit. "Words like tired and phrases like fake enthusiasm were thrown around." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Cultural Impact - Redefining Rock Stardom** : David Bowie profoundly changed culture by subverting the traditional meaning of a rock star, pushing music into new realms of theater and spectacle. His continuously shape-shifting style was widely imitated by artists like Madonna and Lady Gaga, and he served as a crucial inspiration for punk, new wave, post-punk, electronic, goth, industrial, and alternative movements, including bands like the Pixies, Nirvana, Nine Inch Nails, and Arcade Fire. "David Bowie irrevocably changed our culture. He began by subverting what it meant to be a rock star." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

"the death of David Bowie on January 16th, 2016." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nX8uAFDzDYM ← david-bowie
**Death and Posthumous Arrangements (2016)** : David Bowie died peacefully in his sleep at his New York home on Sunday, January 10, 2016, at the age of 69, after an 18-month battle with cancer, having released his final album *Blackstar* just two days prior on his birthday. His death was confirmed by his publicist and son, Duncan Jones, leading to a massive global outpouring of tributes, including 20,000 tweets a minute within an hour. As per his instructions, there was no funeral; he was cremated, and his ashes were taken to Bali for Buddhist rituals, though the exact location where they were spread (possibly Alma Pura or the Sidemen fields, places he loved) remains unknown. "He hung on until this last album was released and his birthday. And then after that, his job was done." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie

His death was unexpected as he had released a critically acclaimed surprise album in 2013 and another acclaimed album just three days before his passing. "David Bowie had suddenly, surprisingly, passed away." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Debut of Ziggy Stardust (July 8, 1972)** : On July 8, 1972, David Bowie introduced the world to his character Ziggy Stardust at the Royal Festival Hall in London. This marked the genesis of the "world's first synthetic, pre-packaged, ultra-theatrical rock star," lasting 360 days and becoming a highly influential piece of marketing and PR in rock history. "That night, David Bowie stepped on stage at the Royal Festival Hall in London and introduced himself by saying, hi, I'm Ziggy." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**Departure from Berlin (Early 1978)** : From early 1978 onwards, David Bowie no longer spent much time living or visiting Berlin, marking a physical and later inspirational detachment from the city. **Departure from Hippie Culture** : Ziggy Stardust marked a distinct departure from the prevailing hippie culture of the 1960s, which was preoccupied with issues like war, environment, advertising, big business, television, and global artificiality. **Departure from Virgin Records (Late 2001)** : David Bowie left Virgin Records in late 2001, reportedly due to a rift caused by the label's disinterest in his "Toy" project, an album of re-recorded early career songs for which they didn't hold the rights. Following his departure, Bowie established his own record label. "This contributed to a rift between the label and Bowie, and in late 2001, he left a set-up as own label." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gdWLtMy4TBU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Early Career Experiments (1967-1969)** : During this period, Bowie extensively experimented to find his artistic niche. **Equipment Theft by Steve Jones (July 1973)** : During a multi-night stand at the Hammersmith Odeon in London in July 1973, David Bowie and The Spiders from Mars had microphones and amplifiers stolen by a young thief named Steve Jones, who later became the guitarist for the Sex Pistols. It is speculated that this stolen gear was used by the Sex Pistols in their early rehearsals and gigs in 1975, contributing to the punk rock era. "When Bowie and the spiders from Mars loaded into the Hammersmith Odien in London in July 1973 for a multi-night stand, a young thief named Steve Jones broke into the theatre and made off with a bunch of microphones and amplifiers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Financial Troubles with Tony DeFrees** : Since the early 1970s, Bowie was entangled in a detrimental management agreement with Tony DeFrees, which left him financially "skint" despite platinum albums and chart-topping singles. Although he parted ways with DeFrees in 1975, the contract allowed DeFrees to collect royalties on Bowie's music until 1996, leading to a protracted legal battle that was a major financial gamble. "Seeing the early 70s, he entered a terrible arrangement with manager Tony DeFrees, and even with all the platinum albums and chart-topping singles, he was close to Skint, he had nothing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Flippant "Gay" Quote (January 1972)** : In January 1972, Bowie gave a flippant quote to a British music paper stating he had "always been gay." This statement was an enormous "bomb" at the time, given that homosexuality had only been decriminalized in Britain for over-21s in England and Wales in 1967, and was still criminalized elsewhere in the UK. This public declaration, despite its flippant nature, profoundly resonated with thousands of gay and confused individuals. "In January, 1972, Bowie gave a flippant quote to a British music paper about having always been gay." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

**Glam Rock Genesis** : David Bowie was significantly inspired by Mark Bolan, a former folk musician who formed the psych band T-Rex. Bolan's appearance on "Top of the Pops" in March 1971, wearing satin clothes covered with glitter dust, struck Bowie as brilliant and marked the beginning of Glam Rock. "This was the beginning of Glam Rock." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Glam Rock Inspirations** : Bowie's full dive into Glam Rock was inspired by Mark Bolan, his "crazy new friend" Iggy Pop, another friend Lou Reed, and a 1968 seven-inch single called "Paralyzed" by "The Legendary Stardust Cowboy." Drawing on his background as an actor and mime, Bowie meticulously experimented with makeup and costuming. "Inspired by Bowen, his crazy new friend Iggy Pop, Lou Reed, another new friend, and a seven inch single from 1968 called Paralyzed by a guy calling himself the legendary Stardust Cowboy. **Glam Rock Pioneer** : David Bowie, particularly during his Ziggy Stardust years, was a pivotal figure in glam rock in the early 1970s. This movement emphasized a glittery, flamboyant look, where clothes and makeup were considered as vital as the music itself in shaping an artist's identity. "glam rock, the glittery, flamboyant look favored by David Bowie and Ziggy Stardust years was as much about the right clothes and the right makeup as it was about music." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mhQ36Y-c9fM ← david-bowie
**Glam Rock Pioneer Misconception** : Contrary to popular belief, David Bowie was not the pioneer of glam music. He was not the first individual to bridge the gap between late 1960s UK music and the 1970s glam movement, nor was *Ziggy Stardust* his first glam album. "David Bowie no fue el pionero de la música glam, él no fue esa primera persona, no fue la persona que conecta la música del reino nido que había en el reino nido a finales de los años 60, con lo que fue el movimiento de la música glam de los años 70." ← Music Radar Clan > EL PIONERO DEL GLAM： MARC BOLAN Y T REX | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Mw_HxfX8iBA&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Glam Rock Transformation - Haircut and Fashion** : Inspired by Marc Bolan, Iggy Pop, Lou Reed, and The Legendary Stardust Cowboy, Bowie went "all in" on glam rock. A key element was his haircut, replicated and modified from a model in a magazine wearing Kansai Yamamoto clothes, razor-cut at the sides and back, backcombed into a "puffy fluff ball," and dyed reddish-orange at Yamamoto's suggestion. This, combined with makeup and costuming, transformed him into the "elfin cute boy in the dress" to something "never before seen in music." "Bowie fun to picture of a model in a magazine." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Golden Period - 1970-1983** : Bowie experienced an incredibly prolific and impactful "golden period" from 1970 to 1983, during which he released 13 albums, many of which became not only classics but milestones in rock history. "He had a golden period that stretched roughly from 1970 through to 1983, 13 albums in those 13 years, and many of them remained not just classics, but milestones in the history of rock." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Groundbreaking Diamond Dogs Tour (1974)** : The tour supporting the "Diamond Dogs" album was one of the most ambitious and expensive rock had ever seen. It featured elaborate sets, costume changes, choreography, and a cherry-picker boom that took Bowie out over the audience during "Space Oddity." This pushed the basic rock and roll show into unprecedented theatrical territory. **Hansa Studio 2 - Berlin** : Bowie and Iggy Pop made music seriously at Hansa Studio 2 in Berlin, located approximately 100 meters from the Berlin Wall, a place where Bowie produced Iggy's album "The Idiot" and recorded two of his own albums. "Berlin also had a very good recording studio called Hansa, all of 100-ish meters from where the Berlin wall ran through the city." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Hansa Studios' Historical Significance** : Studio Two of Hansa Studios, where David Bowie recorded his *Heroes* album, has a unique historical background. The building was originally a concert hall that was later used by the Gestapo as a ballroom during World War II. It was then repurposed into a recording studio by a pair of brothers in 1962. "The building was a former concert hall used by the Gestapo during World War II as a ballroom." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk ← david-bowie
**Heart Attack and Withdrawal (2004)** : In June 2004, while performing at the Hurricane Festival in Germany, Bowie suffered a heart attack caused by a minor coronary artery occlusion, initially mistaken for a pinched nerve. He underwent an emergency angioplasty and, for the first time in his career, canceled a major tour due to health issues. Following his recovery, he largely withdrew from public life. "It was a heart attack right there on stage, caused by a minor coronary artery occlusion, a blocked artery." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Heart Attack in 2005 - Career Slowdown** : In June 2005, while on stage at a festival in Germany, Bowie suffered chest pains, initially misdiagnosed as a pinched nerve. It was later discovered to be a heart attack caused by a blocked coronary artery, requiring emergency angioplasty. This event led to a significant slowdown in his musical output and public appearances, as he became largely invisible, living a quiet life in New York. "In June 2005, it was on stage at a festival in Germany when he started suffering chest pains. It was first diagnosed as a pinched nerve. Later though, it was discovered to have been a heart attack, a blocked coronary artery." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Iconic Haircut and Stylists** : Bowie's new haircut was revolutionary and as historically significant as Elvis's curls or The Beatles' mop tops. Inspired by a model in a magazine wearing designs by Japanese fashion figure Kansai Yamamoto, the cut was replicated on Bowie by stylist Susie Fussy (his mom's hairdresser). It featured razor-cut sides and back, backcombed into a puffy fluff ball, and dyed a bright reddish-orange, transforming him into the "Elfin Cute Boy in the Dress." "Bowie's new haircut was every bit as important to rock history as Elvis's curls or the Beatles mop tops." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

He is described as "the Beatles of the alt rock set." **Influence on Blitz Kids and New Romantics** : David Bowie was highly admired by the Blitz kids, who appreciated his ever-changing sense of style, use of makeup, and gender-bending presentation. His willingness to push boundaries provided a blueprint for their desire for glamour and non-conformity. "And Bowie, in his ever-changing sense of style, and makeup, and drudgedy, gender bending, fantastic for both boys and girls. **Influence on British Punk - Sex Pistols Connection** : Bowie's "outsider-ness," short, sharp songs, wild fashion sense, and defiant attitude endeared him to alienated working-class youth who would become the first generation of British punks. His friendships with Iggy Pop and Lou Reed (of The Velvet Underground) also made him "cool" in their eyes. Famously, on July 2nd, 1973, after Bowie's final Ziggy Stardust tour show at the Hammersmith Odeon, a young Steve Jones (later guitarist for the Sex Pistols) stole microphones and amps from the venue, gear that would be used to start his new band. "A young thief named Steve Jones somehow got inside and helped himself to whatever he could carry out, mostly some microphones and some amps." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

"When she was kicked out of school for her red and pink haircut, she was a big bowie fan." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VnXBJqKwkrw ← david-bowie

**Initial Reaction to Death** : Upon hearing the news of his death, many initially believed it to be an internet hoax, given Bowie's special status and the fact he had just released a new album three days prior. The disbelief stemmed from his recent musical activity and perceived invincibility. "My initial reaction was this surely was another internet hoax. This was Bowie. He was special, probably immortal." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for "Aladdin Sane" Name** : The name for Bowie's new persona, "Aladdin Sane," was a phonetic play on "A Lad Insane," offering a glimpse into his mental state after the intense "Ziggy" experience and his concerns for his half-brother, Terry, who suffered from severe mental health issues. "He called his new image a Latin scene. Separate that to a lad in scene and you'll get the tiniest idea of where his head was at." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for "Bowie" Name** : David Jones chose the name "Bowie" after becoming somewhat obsessed with the character Jim Bowie, played by actor Richard Widmark in the movie "The Alamo." Jim Bowie was a real-life American pioneer, soldier, smuggler, and slave trader famous during the Battle of the Alamo in Texas. "Our David Jones had just seen a movie called The Alamo. He became somewhat obsessed with the character played by actor Richard Widmark. That character's name was Jim Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for "Space Oddity" - Stanley Kubrick & Garden Gnomes** : Bowie was heavily influenced by Stanley Kubrick's "2001, A Space Odyssey," which he saw while "stoned out of his mind" in 1968, leading to the creation of "Space Oddity." The character name "Major Tom" might also have been inspired by Tom Major, the father of future British Prime Minister John Major, who had a second career making garden gnomes. "But it's possible that the name of the character in the song was inspired by the story of a failed British trapezoid artist named Tom Major." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for Dark Music** : David Bowie was identified as one of the artists whose dark music attracted punk refugees, influencing the nascent Goth scene. "That would include David Bowie and joint-evision, the first version of Ultravox, and an Irish performance art group called The Virgin Proons." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gd9sO7c3N1s ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for LGBTQ+ Individuals** : Bowie's public comments about his sexuality in 1972 struck a chord with thousands who were afraid to come out, giving them courage and a sense of shared identity with a famous figure. Figures like Boy George of Culture Club and Holly Johnson of Frankie Goes to Hollywood have stated that Bowie's comments changed their lives. "Bowie gave them the courage to be who they were." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Inspiration for Ziggy Stardust** : David Bowie's iconic Ziggy Stardust character was partly inspired by Iggy Pop's persona, influencing the choice of the name "Ziggy." "That character was to be in part inspired by Iggy. I mean, why do you think Bowie chose the name Ziggy?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w-rihv544I8 ← david-bowie
**Inspiration from Marc Bolan** : Bowie was significantly inspired by Marc Bolan of T-Rex. Bolan's stage attitude, aesthetic, and musical compositions deeply influenced Bowie's work in the 1970s, making him a central figure of inspiration. "Siempre se recuerda como la persona que inspiraba David Bowie." ← Music Radar Clan > EL PIONERO DEL GLAM： MARC BOLAN Y T REX | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Mw_HxfX8iBA&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Inspired by "Shame Shame Shame"** : David Bowie was inspired by Shirley & Company's "Shame Shame Shame" to rework a song he and Carlos Alomar had been working on, titled "Footstump," transforming it into the hit "Fame." "That's the song that inspired David Bowie, John Lennon, and Carlos Alema to re-work a song Bowie and Alema had been working on called Footstump him into fame." ← Episode 49： ＂Love is Strange＂ by Mickey and Sylvia | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FkyLPVvPbcI
**Inspired by Giorgio Moroder** : David Bowie was notably inspired by the electronic music innovations of Giorgio Moroder. Moroder's experimental work with synthesizers and his unique sound influenced Bowie's own musical explorations. "Even Bowie was inspired by Moroder." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zIkjd1OjCXM ← david-bowie
**International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments** : In November 1964, David Jones appeared on a BBC News program as the founder, president, and spokesman for this organization. Its purpose was to advocate for the social acceptance of young British men wearing long hair. "The first time anyone really heard about him was when he appeared on a BBC News program in November of 1964 as the founder, president, and spokesman for the International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6oUkMOkEr9U ← david-bowie

**Interview in Jeremy Magazine (1970)** : In January 1970, David Bowie became one of the first pop stars to be interviewed by Jeremy, a gay magazine. Although the article itself did not focus on his sexuality, the mere fact of his appearance in a gay publication was considered radical, especially given that just three years prior, being gay was still a jailable offense in the UK. "the very fact that he appeared in a game egg was pretty radical." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hswtuenFwvM ← david-bowie

**Ironic Quotation Marks for "Heroes"** : David Bowie treated the song and album "Heroes" with detachment, intentionally putting ironic quotation marks around the title. This "arch gesture" meant both the song and the album were officially called, "quote, heroes, unquote," even though the song is now unironically beloved and recognized as a global anthem. "Even Boey treated the song with detachment, putting ironic quotation marks around the title. Officially, both the song and the album are called, quote, heroes, unquote." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7

His death marked the end of a career that spanned six decades and profoundly influenced music and culture. "David Bowie, who passed away on January 10th, 2016, just two days after his 69th birthday." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Kanye West Prediction Theory** : A conspiracy theory claims David Bowie predicted the rise of Kanye West back in 1972. Proponents cite Bowie's *Ziggy Stardust and the Spiders from Mars* album (released June 16, 1972) and its song "Five Years" as foretelling the event, noting Kanye's birth on June 8, 1977, almost five years later. The theory also highlights the "K. West" sign visible on the *Ziggy Stardust* album cover (from a fur store), interpreting it as a direct reference, and Bowie's final album, *Black Star*, as an "anointment" of Kanye, referred to as a "Black Star." Bowie's known visionary capabilities regarding digital music, social media, and gender fluidity are used to support his ability to predict Kanye's ascendance. "Did David Bowie predict the rise of Kanye West way back in 1972?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pmKjZzypzvg ← david-bowie
**Killing Off Ziggy Stardust (1973)** : At the end of the 1973 Ziggy Stardust tour, Bowie announced to the audience that it would be "the last show that we'll ever do." While the public thought he was retiring, Bowie intended to retire the Ziggy persona to make way for a new one, Aladdin Sane. This willingness to "kill himself off" and constantly reinvent was admired by punks. "What he really meant though was that he was killing off Ziggy." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Kraftwerk Influence** : Bowie's three albums created in Berlin with Brian Eno were explicitly "Kraftwerk inspired." These works showcased a belief that electronics represented a viable and important path forward for musical innovation. "He created three craftwork inspired albums with producer Brian Eno that show that maybe electronics were the way for." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=iL9KpQFqH4o ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Krautrock and Berlin Influence** : David Bowie was profoundly "shaken and inspired" by early Krautrock, especially Kraftwerk, which led him to move to Berlin. This period resulted in three of his most fascinating albums: "Low," "Heroes," and "Lodger," with the B-side of the "Heroes" single, "V-2 Schneider," directly named after Florian Schneider. "David Bowie was so shaken and inspired by early crop rock and craftwork in particular, as he moved to Berlin and made three of his most fascinating albums as a result." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ePZDkqLM_gw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Lack of Formal Musical Training** : Bowie did not possess formal musical training, unlike many of his contemporaries. This was viewed as a positive attribute, as it allowed him to avoid the constraints of conventional musical "rules." "Sometimes it helps to not be constrained by what you think the rules are." ← For the Record - The 70s > Ep. 26 - Starmen - Glam Rock of the 70s | https://seventies.libsyn.com/026-glam-11820-6-34-pm

**Last Public Appearance (December 7, 2015)** : David Bowie made his final public appearance on December 7, 2015, attending the opening night of "Lazarus," a play for which he wrote the music and lyrics, at the New York Theater Workshop in Manhattan. Although too ill to attend rehearsals, he felt compelled to be present for the premiere. "The last time he was seen in public was on December 7, 2015. He had written the music and lyrics for a play called Lazarus, and he was there for opening night at the new theater workshop in Manhattan." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hhii2_BVE7A ← david-bowie
**Late 1980s Creative Reassessment** : After facing disappointment with albums like "Tonight" (1984) and "Never Let Me Down" (1987), Bowie decided to "switch gears again" in 1988, recognizing that hard rock would move away from hair metal towards a more primal sound. He aimed to make music he personally enjoyed, rather than chasing audience preferences. "So Bowie decided to switch gears again. In 1988, he saw how the way the wind was blowing. Heavy and hard rock was going to move away from hair metal and into something more primal over the next few years. Bowie was into this music at the time and wanted to pursue this sound. Instead of chasing what audiences wanted, he was once again to make music that he liked." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cy5SCQV0HAY ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Late Touring Career Rider – Minimalist Demands** : In the late stages of his touring career, David Bowie became remarkably undemanding. His rider simply asked for a fruit bowl and that his dressing room be maintained at a specific temperature, between 14 and 18 degrees Celsius. "All he asked for was a fruit bowl and that he required his dressing room to be kept at a temperature between 14 and 18 degrees Celsius." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=z2hvUDtBxho ← david-bowie

"In 1985, it was Bowie to the Rescue again. After listening to some rough tapes of some new songs, he encouraged Iggy and his new buddy, ex-sex pistol guitar Steve Jones, to make another album." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OxctiPr0l-8 ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Leading Visionary of Rock (Late 1970s)** : As the 1970s drew to a close, Bowie was widely regarded as the leading visionary in rock music. He was consistently several steps ahead of his contemporaries, possessing acute instincts for future trends, or perhaps, actively shaping the direction in which he wanted music to evolve. "He was always several steps ahead of everybody else. And his instincts for what was to come next were bang on." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

**Liberating Aesthetic Against Stereotypes** : He is considered an icon of culture who promoted a philosophy where "what you are doesn't matter, but what you feel and what makes you happy, and that you don't have to name things." This informed much of his aesthetic, which was very liberating, allowing men for the first time to dress like women, not be masculine, or not fit into existing stereotypes without being linked to specific sexual orientations. He was a great step forward against sexual stereotypes. "Que la llevó muchísimo a toda su estética y que fue una estética muy liberadora, porque por primera vez podíamos tener hombres que se desquien con mujeres o que no querían ser masculinos o que no querían encajar dentro de estos estereotipos y no por ello tenían que estar vinculados a unas opciones sexuales o a otras." ← Music Radar Clan > Artistas gays que cambiaron nuestra sociedad. | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=85SJzsll27U&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

Due to immigration and work permit issues, he was unable to officially tour for *The Man Who Sold the World*, instead conducting private concerts for journalists from his hotel room bed. **Liver Cancer Diagnosis - Final Album** : In the summer of 2014, Bowie began feeling unwell and was diagnosed with liver cancer, which was initially treatable. Knowing he likely had time for only one more album, he began writing songs that would serve as his own "eulogy" or "requiem," leading to the creation of "Blackstar." "Bowie had been feeling unwell. **Los Angeles Cocaine Psychosis (1970s) – Station to Station Blackout** : During his mid-1970s Los Angeles period, David Bowie survived almost exclusively on milk, red peppers, and cocaine, which induced extreme paranoia. He believed he was being monitored by aliens, surrounded himself with Egyptian protective artifacts, and played his records backward searching for hidden messages. He has stated he has no memory whatsoever of recording the album *Station to Station*. **MTV Racism Challenge (1983)** : In 1983, David Bowie confronted MTV VJ Mark Goodman in an interview, calling out the channel's "subtle racism" for featuring very few Black artists, particularly during prime daytime hours. He observed that while many Black artists were making excellent videos, they were rarely aired on MTV, in contrast to a dedicated Black music station. "I'm just flawed by the fact that there's so many so few black artists featured on it. **Mainstream Crossover Success (1975)** : By 1975, with the "Young Americans" album, Bowie had become a global superstar whose music transcended genre boundaries. **Manager Tony DeFries (Late 1970s)** : In the late 1970s, David Bowie acquired Tony DeFries as his manager, who actively supported Bowie's search for new artistic approaches to rock music, including his decision to wear a dress in public. "In the late 1970s, he acquired a new manager, a character by the name of Tony DeFries." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie
**Manager Tony DeFries and Image Transformation** : Bowie's new manager, Tony DeFries, believed that for Bowie to succeed, he needed a provocative image and a weird brand marketed alongside his music. DeFries encouraged Bowie to experiment with makeup and costumes, a plan Bowie embraced. He acquired long, flowing, and expensive gowns from a designer named Mr. Fish, continuing a tendency to dress to shock that dated back to his mod days in high school. "DeFries encouraged Bowie to experiment with makeup and costumes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie
**Manager Tony DeFries' Early Guidance (1970-1972)** : Tony DeFries, a solicitor by profession, signed on as Bowie's manager in 1970 when Bowie was a struggling young singer. Within approximately 18 months, DeFries secured Bowie a new deal with RCA records and proceeded to transform him into an international star. The entirety of Bowie's early 1970s career, including the iconic Ziggy Stardust era, was carefully guided by DeFries. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=PzyvXmDKFUc ← david-bowie

**Melody Maker Interview (January 1972)** : In early 1972, Bowie gave a front-page interview to British music weekly Melody Maker, titled "Oh, You Pretty Thing." The article described his image as a "swishy queen, a gorgeously effeminate boy," noting his "camp" demeanor while he maintained he was "ungay." This interview showcased his deliberate push for shocking outrage and sexual ambiguity. "He gave an interview to Melody Maker, one of the big British music weeklies. The title of the article was, oh, you pretty thing." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Mid-70s Drug Addiction and Paranoia** : In the mid-1970s, Bowie struggled with heavy drinking and tremendous amounts of cocaine, often eating little more than milk and peppers. This period led to erratic behavior, such as storing urine in his fridge out of fear that "unspecified witches" would steal his "vital essence," and touring with a telescope, convinced that aliens in an orbiting mothership were coming for him. He later stated he had no recollection of anything that happened in 1976. "But the truth was the boy was drinking heavily and using tremendous amounts of cocaine while eating little more than milk and peppers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Move to Berlin - Cold War Artistic Hub** : In an effort to escape the negative influences surrounding him in L.A. and kick his cocaine addiction, Bowie and Iggy Pop moved to Berlin, Germany. During the height of the Cold War, Berlin was a divided city, yet its unique artistic and bohemian culture provided the perfect environment for Bowie's musical evolution, where he immersed himself in German electronic and crude rock sounds. "He and Iggy Pop packed up and left for Berlin. Now Berlin. Nobody went to Berlin. This was the height of the Cold War." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Move to Berlin for Recovery (1976)** : To recover from his drug addiction and escape the intense spotlight of Los Angeles, David Bowie decided to move away. After a temporary stop in Switzerland, he relocated to Berlin with his friend Iggy Pop. "Para recuperarse y escapar del foco de atención, decide huir de los ángeles que su amigo y hip-hop." ← El proyecto que salvó a David Bowie. **Move to West Berlin for Sobriety (Post-1976)** : Following his period of intense drug addiction and paranoia, Bowie, along with Iggy Pop, made a conscious decision to move to West Berlin to get sober, clean up, and dry out, seeking clarity from his drug-induced state. "It wasn't until he and Iggy Pop had a moment of clarity and decided that they needed to move to West Berlin to clean up, get sober and dry out." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU ← david-bowie
**Move to West Berlin with Iggy Pop** : Deeply influenced by German electronic groups like Kraftwerk, Can, and Neu!, and envisioning electronic music as the future, Bowie moved to West Berlin with Iggy Pop to immerse themselves in the local scene and simultaneously recover from their addictions. They settled in a modest place at Hopstresser 155 in the Schöneberg area, motivated by a belief that remaining in Los Angeles would lead to their demise. "He began to think that these electronic methods of producing music were the future. And what better way to follow this muse than to move to where it all seemed to be happening? Germany." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

He continuously listened to *To Pimp a Butterfly* during the recording of his final album, *Blackstar*, which drew significant inspiration and parallels from Lamar's work. "Tony, esto es lo que yo quiero hacer. **NME Interview Coming Out (1972)** : On January 22nd, 1972, Bowie gave an interview to the NME, a major British weekly music tabloid, where he famously stated, "I'm gay and I always have been." While later acknowledged as a publicity stunt, the impact of those seven words was immense and incalculable, giving hope to closeted individuals globally. "I'm gay and I always have been." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hswtuenFwvM ← david-bowie
**Naked in Bed with Mick Jagger – Angela Bowie's 1990 TV Claim, Denied Then Partially Walked Back** : On May 4, 1990, David Bowie's ex-wife Angela appeared on the Joan Rivers Show, newly freed from a 10-year gag order after their divorce. She stated on national television: "I caught him in bed with Mick Jagger — and yes, they were naked." Bowie was a professed bisexual during the 1970s. Mick Jagger immediately dismissed the claim as "rubbish," and Bowie's lawyer sent an open letter stating that "any implication that there was ever a gay affair between Mick Jagger and David Bowie is an absolute fabrication." Within a week, Angela was qualifying her statement. By her 1993 autobiography, the account had evolved: she had walked in, assumed they had been having sex, and that was her honest belief, but she had no proof. An additional complication: Angela may have had her own affair with Jagger during the marriage, possibly inspiring the Rolling Stones song "Angie" — or, in another rumor, that "Angie" referred to David himself using a nickname. "Did they spend the night together? Yes. Were they naked? Apparently. Was it sexual? Who knows?" ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GIUTQhcmR5s ← david-bowie
**Name Change Motivation** : David Jones changed his name to David Bowie to avoid confusion with two other notable figures: a poet and painter of some renown in South London also named David Jones, and David Jones, the short kid who moved to America and joined the TV band The Monkees. "First, there was a poet and painter of some renowned and South London named David Jones. And then there was that short kid who moved to America and joined a TV band called The Monkeys." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Name Change to Avoid Confusion (1966)** : In 1966, David Jones changed his name to David Bowie to prevent being confused with Davey Jones, the "cute little English dude" from the popular TV show, The Monkees. "In 1966, David Jones would change his name to David Bowie to avoid being confused with Davey Jones, who was the cute little English dude on the TV show The Monkeys." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6oUkMOkEr9U ← david-bowie
**Name Change to David Bowie** : David Jones changed his name to David Bowie due to the existence of other notable David Joneses, including a poet/painter and Dave Jones of The Monkees. He was inspired by the character Jim Bowie, a real-life American pioneer, soldier, smuggler, and slave trader famous from the Battle of the Alamo, played by Richard Widmark in the movie "The Alamo." The correct pronunciation is "Bowie," not "Bowie." "So henceforth, David Jones began calling himself David Bowie, not Bowie, but Bowie." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**New York City Residence** : After his 2004 heart attack, Bowie lived a reclusive life in a luxurious penthouse at 285 Lafayette Street in New York City's Soho Nolita area. The 5,100-square-foot residence featured direct elevator access, 11-foot ceilings, a large library, four bedrooms, four bathrooms, and three terraces. He occasionally went out, sometimes with his wife and daughter, and enjoyed Washington Square Park. He used disguises like sunglasses, a hat, and carrying a Greek language newspaper to deter recognition. "As you might expect, it was a lovely place, filled with fine, expensive art, tastefully decorated, and with an interior crafted by architects and designers from Europe." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie

**Numerous Honors and Legacy** : Bowie is enshrined in the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame, the Songwriter's Hall of Fame, and the Science Fiction and Fantasy Hall of Fame. The BBC once named him the best-dressed Briton in history. A species of spider, an asteroid (342843 David Bowie), and British postal stamps have been named in his honor. A statue of him stands in Ailsbury, UK, where he first introduced Ziggy Stardust, and a street in Paris bears his name. "I think I could go on, but I probably have made my point." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Obsession with Hitler and Nazi Sympathies (Mid-1970s)** : Bowie developed a dangerous obsession with Hitler and the Third Reich during his drug-addled period, frequently discussing Nazis in interviews. In 1976, he controversially told Playboy magazine that Hitler was one of the first rock stars, and was seen giving what appeared to be a Nazi salute to a crowd at a London train station. "And if that wasn't enough, Bowie had become obsessed with Hitler and the Third Reich." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU ← david-bowie
**Obsession with Witches and Bodily Fluids (1974-1976)** : During his period of intense drug use and paranoia, Bowie became convinced that "witches" were trying to steal his "precious bodily fluids." To prevent this, he began saving all his urine in a fridge and maintained a strict diet of bell peppers and milk to keep his "essence pure," leading his weight to drop below 90 pounds. "Specifically, he got it into his mind that witches, that's as specific as we can get, were out to steal Bowie's precious bodily fluids." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dVJuITJyNTU ← david-bowie

**Patronage of Iggy Pop and The Stooges** : Bowie was a great admirer and musical hero of Iggy Pop, fascinated by his craziness, almost constant mental instability, and ability to see beyond the drugs and self-destructive stage antics to Iggy's intelligence. Bowie convinced his manager to take on Iggy and The Stooges as a project, providing a cash injection that funded their *Raw Power* album. He later visited Iggy when he was in a mental hospital. Bowie's acceptance of Iggy also helped propel the first three Stooges albums to become important templates for punk rock. "Iggy's craziness had made him into one of Bowie's musical heroes." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie
**Patronage of Lou Reed** : Bowie was also a great admirer of Lou Reed and The Velvet Underground, recognizing Reed's talent despite him being on the fringes and largely unknown. Bowie offered his patronage, leading him to produce Reed's 1972 album *Transformer*, collaborating with his Spiders From Mars guitarist, Mick Ronson, to help Reed find a new sound. "Bowie did, though, and he offered to lend his patronage to Lou." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie

**Personal Struggles (Mid-1970s)** : Despite his global superstardom, Bowie was in a terrible personal state in the mid-1970s. Paradoxically, these struggles did not diminish his influence, but rather made him appear even more mysterious and, consequently, bigger. **Personal and Career Reset in Berlin (1977)** : Prompted by his raging addiction and a need to change his trajectory, Bowie left America and England for West Berlin in 1977. **Pioneer of Digital Distribution** : David Bowie demonstrated foresight regarding the digital future of music by releasing his "Hours" album on September 21st, 1999, making it the first album by a major artist legally available for online download two weeks before its physical release. "Some like David Bowie saw a digital future coming. **Pop Success as a "Costume"** : Bowie approached pop success as "one more cloak to try on and then discard," treating pop stardom like a costume. This contrasted with artists like Lou Reed or Joni Mitchell, who found that experimentation often led to commercial toxicity, while Bowie successfully experimented and scored hits before, during, and after his artistic explorations, setting a new template for shape-shifters with pop aspirations. "For Bowie, pop success was one more cloak to try on and then discard." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7
**Post-"Let's Dance" Creative Struggles** : The immense success of "Let's Dance" unexpectedly confused Bowie, making him feel detached from his audience and uncertain of their expectations. This "confused headspace" initiated a creative downturn for the rest of the 1980s, as his subsequent work was unfairly judged against the commercial peak of "Let's Dance." "I suddenly felt very apart from my audience and it was depressing because I didn't know what they wanted." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Post-1976 Influence on Goth** : David Bowie's music, particularly everything he released after 1976, played a role in coalescing the darker-minded punk scene, influencing the emergence of goth. His glam-era style from ten years prior was also a significant inspiration at The Batcave club. "This is where David Bowie turns up again, especially everything he released after 1976." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XaLsZFLrMnI ← david-bowie

**Post-Berlin Trilogy Career Shift** : Over three years, David Bowie cleaned himself up and achieved new artistic goals with the Berlin Trilogy, though he distanced himself from mainstream pop success. At the dawn of the 1980s, he began to make his way back onto the charts, aiming to fully re-enter the pop landscape on his own terms, a strategic pivot that would help define the next wave of New Wave music. "So, over the course of three years, Boey had cleaned himself up and achieved new artistic goals with the Berlin Trilogy, but divorced himself from pop success." ← Hit Parade Music History and Music Trivia > Starman to Blackstar Edition Part 1 | https://shows.acast.com/hit-parade/episodes/696aa42a4796fcbb571adba7

**Post-Death World Deterioration** : Many people observed a noticeable decline in global affairs after Bowie's death, leading to a "meme" that the world "kind of started going a hell" after he died. This includes political, social, economic, and technological shifts like Brexit, Putin's actions, the Ukraine conflict, COVID, Gaza, and the rise of AI. "I'm sure it's all a coincidence, but it's no exaggeration to say that since Bowie died, we've transitioned into a completely different world." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Post-Heart Attack Seclusion and Subsequent Heart Attacks** : The heart attack scare in 2004 prompted David Bowie to re-evaluate his life, leading him to live in seclusion for the remainder of his life. It is reported that he experienced at least another five heart attacks between 2004 and his death in 2016. "But that heart attack scare caused him to re-evaluate everything. He chose to live in seclusion for the rest of his life. And word is that he had at least another five heart attacks between 2004 and 2016." ← Ongoing History of New Music > People Who (Almost) Died | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7rXwaxlEkbQ&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Post-Let's Dance Audience Alienation** : Following the immense commercial success of "Let's Dance," Bowie felt a profound sense of alienation from his new audience, questioning their connection to his artistic roots. This psychological impact marked the beginning of a creative "spiral" that continued throughout the rest of the 1980s, as his subsequent work was often judged against his previous innovations. "I remember looking out over these waves of people who were coming to hear this record played live and thinking, I wonder how many velvet underground albums these people have in their record collections. I suddenly felt very apart from my audience, and it was depressing because I didn't know what they wanted." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Post-Tin Machine Return to Solo Career** : After Tin Machine broke up in 1992, David Bowie reverted to his solo identity, achieving "decent success," though not on the same scale as his iconic 1970s and early 1980s period. "After Tin Machine broke up in 1992, David Bowie went back to being, well, David Bowie. He had some decent success, but nothing like what we saw in the 70s and early 80s." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cy5SCQV0HAY ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Posthumous Critical Re-evaluation** : The posthumous success of Black Star, reaching No. 1 on charts and receiving awards, significantly altered the perception of David Bowie's later career. Previously, albums like *Hitin*, *Hours*, and *Reality* had faced criticism regarding their musical quality, but Black Star's impact led to a re-evaluation, solidifying his final work as a significant artistic legacy. "Resulta triste que a David Bowie le añandado el número 1 en todas las listas y le añandado todos estos premios postumos cuando los últimos albumes de la carrera de David Bowie sobre todo los últimos tres, cuatro albumes, el hitin, el hours, el reality, habían sido un tanto cuestionado por su calidad musical." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Prague Concert Abrupt End (June 23, 2004)** : During his Prague concert on June 23, 2004, David Bowie's performance was severely affected by his heart attack. After an attempt to play "Station to Station" which started and stopped, everyone left the stage. Ten minutes later, Bowie and the band returned to try and finish the song, then performed "The Man Who Sold the World," but "Changes" ended after its intro, effectively concluding the show. "It started and stopped. And that was it. Everybody left the stage. Ten minutes later, Bowie and the band were back to try to finish the song. Then they went into the man who sold the world. And then they started changes but ended after the intro." ← Ongoing History of New Music > People Who (Almost) Died | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7rXwaxlEkbQ&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Profound Influence** : David Bowie is considered one of the most influential musicians ever, arguably influencing more musical genres than even The Beatles due to his constant reinvention. His artistic DNA can be found across glam, punk, art rock, folk, hard rock, grunge, industrial music, electronic music, indie rock, and hip-hop. He brought an unprecedented level of sophistication to rock music, and his work continues to be studied, finding new fans across generations. "His DNA can be found in glam, punk, art rock folk, hard rock, grunge, industrial music, electronic music of all flavors, indie rock, and hip-hop." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie

**Prolific Abstract Painting** : During his 1976 esthetic phase, David Bowie became a prolific painter, producing thousands of abstract and "esthetic" pictures, often completing them in as little as five minutes. He painted continuously, creating a vast body of work, though the quality and complexity of these quickly produced pieces were not noted as exceptional. "pintaba de mayor composición miles de cuadros pero miles continuamente cuadros un poco abstractos y esténicos que le pintaban cinco minutos pero no paraba." ← Music Radar Clan > Pedro y el lobo de David Bowie | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Hqx7Ev9NDJY&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Prolific Output (1970s)** : Bowie's rise to stardom was characterized by an incredible prolificness, releasing "album after album, single after single, character after character, tour after tour." This constant stream of new material was remarkable, especially as his records were commercial and critical successes and each was distinct from the last, creating immense mystery and public curiosity. "That prolificness was a big part of Bowie's rise to start him." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Prolific Output and Reinvention (1973-1975)** : Between 1973 and 1975, Bowie released an astonishing six albums in just three years and two months, including "Aladdin Sane," "Pin Ups," "Diamond Dogs," "David Live," and "Young Americans." Each record was different, making every release an event and keeping audiences guessing what Bowie would do next. "Album after album, single after single character after character two or after two or it was absolutely incredible." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Prolific Output in the 70s/80s** : From "Hunky Dory" onward, Bowie released 11 studio albums and two live albums in just over eight and a half years. During this intense period, he also collaborated with artists like Iggy Pop, survived a deep cocaine addiction, and expanded his artistic endeavors into film and theater, taking on projects that regular rock stars typically avoided. "He did, however, predict pretty much everything that would happen with music with the rise of the Internet. Here's what he said in 1999, just as the Internet was starting to go mainstream. **Public Declaration of Sexuality** : In January 1972, Bowie publicly professed to be gay in an interview in *Melody Maker* magazine. This statement was far more scandalous in 1970s Britain than his earlier cross-dressing, as homosexuality had only been decriminalized in the UK in 1967. This declaration made his previous dress-wearing seem "minuscule." "The big media storm came when Bowie publicly professed to be gay in an interview in Melody Maker magazine in January of 1972." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie
**Public Homosexuality Confession (1972)** : On January 22, 1972, David Bowie made a shocking declaration to a British music tabloid reporter, stating, "I'm gay and I always have been." While such a statement is common today, in 1972, it was highly controversial and made him the first major rock and roll musician to publicly profess his homosexuality. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z9T9wi0vEvc ← david-bowie

**Recording of Peter and the Wolf Narration (1976)** : In 1976, at the height of his mystical and esthetic ravings, Bowie conceived the idea to record Sergei Prokofiev's classical work *Peter and the Wolf*.
