**Relationship with Mick Jagger** : In the early 1970s, David Bowie and Mick Jagger, both known for sexual experimentation, became close friends after a 1973 Bowie concert. They were frequently seen together in public, including clubs, concerts, and even at a Muhammad Ali fight, with one biographer crediting Bowie for introducing Jagger to gay culture. Bowie's backup singer, Aiba Cherry, claimed the two were "sexually obsessed with each other" and she witnessed them having sex, with associates confirming their close relationship during which they "practically lived together for several months." David's ex-wife, Angela Bowie, claimed on the Joan Rivers show in 1990 that she caught them naked and asleep in bed together. "Mick and Dave were really sexually obsessed with each other. Even though I was in bed with them many times, I ended up just watching them have sex. **Rumored Affair with Mick Jagger (1990)** : A long-standing rumor regarding an affair between David Bowie and Mick Jagger originated on the Joan Rivers show on May 4, 1990. Angela Bowie, David's ex-wife (married 1970-1980), claimed on the show, after a decade-long gag order from her divorce settlement expired, that she caught them naked in bed together. Bowie had professed bisexuality in the 1970s, which lent some credibility to the story. Mick Jagger vehemently denied the claims, and Bowie's lawyer issued a letter calling any implication of a gay affair an "absolute fabrication." Angela Bowie later revised her story in her 1993 autobiography, stating she "just assumed they were having sex" and lacked proof. "I caught David in bed with Mick Jagger." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DA2iJsu3GRY ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Secret Comeback (2011-2013)** : Bowie orchestrated his 2013 comeback album, *The Next Day*, in absolute secrecy. He worked with trusted producer Tony Visconti and a small coterie of musicians, all of whom signed non-disclosure agreements. His family and the skeleton staff at The Magic Shop studio (near his apartment) kept the secret. He had minimal staff, only his fiercely loyal personal assistant Coco Schwab and business person Bill Zysblat, with no pressure from his record label, Sony. His understanding of the internet meant he knew he could announce his return without a traditional marketing campaign, simply by dropping a hint online. "How did Bowie, one of the most famous musicians in the world that ever seen, manage that? He was working with Tony Visconti again. Tony can keep a secret." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Yq2A_o9-ulM ← david-bowie
**Secret Messages in Music (early-mid 1970s)** : Bowie was convinced he was trying to send secret messages to himself through his music. To uncover these, he had a special turntable custom-made, which allowed him to listen to his own records played backwards. "He had a special turntable made so we could listen to his own records backwards because Bowie was convinced he was sending secret messages to himself." ← Ongoing History of New Music > Alt Rocks Craziest People | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=CgReNKciFJo&list=PLM8bxV0E1Gse5C3n1u-mkVSTZLL5AJICG ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Secret Recording of "The Next Day"** : Bowie managed to record his album "The Next Day" in complete secrecy over two years in the internet age, a feat considered miraculous. This was achieved through the unwavering loyalty of his associates, who were sworn to secrecy, and by Bowie living a remarkably low-key life in New York City with Iman. He was often seen walking, grocery shopping, and attending social events, but people were accustomed to his flamboyant personas and simply didn't notice "David Jones." "How could one of the most famous musicians in the history of the universe manage to record an album in total secrecy in the age of the internet? **Severe Addiction and Health Crisis - 1975-1976** : During the period from late 1975 to late 1976, Bowie was heavily drinking and consuming tremendous amounts of cocaine, while subsisting on little more than milk and peppers. His weight plummeted to less than 90 pounds, indicating a severe health crisis, and he was described as "cracking up." "Bowie was drinking very heavily and using tremendous amounts of cocaine while eating a little more than milk and peppers." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rw0uXf5UJvo ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Sexual Identity Declaration (1972)** : Six months before the release of *The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and The Spiders from Mars*, David Bowie declared himself to be gay. Given that homosexuality had only been decriminalized in England in 1967, this public confession from a major pop star had a huge liberating effect on individuals afraid to reveal their own sexual orientation. "Six months before the album came, a Bowie declared himself to be gay." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dm5N6yDRxXQ ← david-bowie
**Shape-Shifting Persona and Identity** : Bowie embraced being different offstage from his onstage personas, unlike many rock artists who strive for authenticity. He curated characters like Ziggy Stardust, Aladdin Sane, Halloween Jack, the plastic soul man, and the Thin White Duke, frequently changing his image and character to capture public imagination and drive his artistic evolution. "It's very hard to convince people that you can be quite different offstage in rock and more than you are onstage." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Songs Revert to Bowie (2007)** : When the Bowie Bonds hit junk status in 2007, the songs and their income reverted back to David Bowie, making his initial $55 million gamble a win. "2007, Bowie swoops in, and the songs revert back to him along with their income. So Bowie made a $55 million bet, and he won." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Pe40SqDrpZ0 ← david-bowie
**Sound + Vision Tour - Retiring Hits** : To shed the "baggage" of his past successes and start fresh, Bowie undertook the Sound + Vision Tour, during which he promised to play his old hits like "Space Oddity," "Ziggy Stardust," "Rebel Rebel," "Young Americans," "Heroes," and "Let's Dance" one last time before retiring them forever. His intention was to clear the decks and move forward creatively. "The first was something called the Sound Invision Tour where Bowie promised to play his old hits one more time and then retire them forever." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Spider Species** : A spider species, *headropodid David Bowie*, has been named after David Bowie. This spider is found in Malaysia and is characterized by being large, yellow, and hairy. "Lusefran David Bowie has his own spider, headropodid David Bowie, which lives in Malaysia." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=VMPLplhDk8I ← david-bowie
**Spokesman for International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments** : In the early 1960s, before achieving widespread fame, David Bowie (then David Jones) acted as a spokesman for a group called the International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments, advocating for men's right to wear long hair. "In the early 1960s, long before anybody knew who he was, Bowie was a spokesman for a group called the International League for the Preservation of Animal Filaments." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Steve Jones' Theft of Bowie's Gear (July 3, 1973)** : Following Bowie's final Ziggy Stardust show at the Hammersmith Odeon in London on July 2, 1973, a young thief named Steve Jones (who would later form The Sex Pistols) broke into the venue. While a night watchman slept, Jones stole microphones, amps, and cymbals, some of which would be used to start his new band. "A young thief named Steve Jones somehow got inside and managed to help himself to whatever he could carry out, mostly some microphones and some amps along with a couple of symbols." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Stolen Microphones Used by Sex Pistols** : During a Ziggy Stardust performance in London, thugs broke in after the show and stole all the band's microphones. One of these thieves was Steve Jones, who subsequently used those very microphones in his new band, the Sex Pistols. "One of those thieves was a kid named Steve Jones, and those mics were literally used in his new band called the Sex Pistols." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Dm5N6yDRxXQ ← david-bowie
**Strategic Catalog Lease During Internet Upheaval** : Bowie leased his catalog for a 10-year period just before the internet "nearly destroyed the recorded music industry." This strategic timing allowed him to avoid financial losses from music piracy and declining CD sales, collecting a payday of $55 million. At the end of the term, he regained ownership and began earning money through streaming, owning everything by his death in 2016. "What's even more remarkable was his timing. He leased his catalog for a period of 10 years just before the internet nearly destroyed the recorded music industry. And while everyone else was losing money because of music piracy and dropping CD sales, Roy laughed all the way to the bank with a payday of $55 million." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cy5SCQV0HAY ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Struggles and Move to West Berlin (May 1976)** : Living in Los Angeles had severely impacted David Bowie's sanity, leaving him in a fog of alcohol and cocaine abuse. He developed severe paranoia, believing aliens were coming to collect him, and reportedly collected his urine in jars as protection against alien abduction. Recognizing the need for a change, Bowie moved to West Berlin in late May 1976 with Iggy Pop to detoxify and regenerate amidst the city's bohemian and unconventional inhabitants. "Living in LA had seriously jeopardized their sanity." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AymMybE33zU ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Struggling for Image and Sound (Late 1960s)** : Around the time The Velvet Underground, The Stooges, MC5, and Captain Beefheart were making records, David Bowie was struggling to define his own image, style, and sound, without much success. "Well, he was trying to find himself. He was trying to come up with an image and a style and a sound that would work for him and he wasn't doing very well." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=6oUkMOkEr9U ← david-bowie

Far from damaging his career, this "simple, albeit untrue, statement" paradoxically enhanced his mystique and boosted his popularity. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z9T9wi0vEvc ← david-bowie

**Swiss Residence and Obsessions** : Around the time he seemed to be at his lowest point, David Bowie moved to a millionaire house by a lake in Switzerland, which offered him a "hermetismo" or sense of privacy. During this period, he developed intense obsessions with painting (creating several canvases daily, often unfinished), contemporary art (amassing one of the world's most important collections), photography, dance, and classical music, seeking out expensive teachers for these pursuits. "se muda a una casa millonaria en suiza. **Terminal Illness Kept Secret** : During the recording of Black Star, David Bowie was suffering from a terminal illness, a fact known only to his long-time producer and friend, Tony Visconti. The other musicians and collaborators involved in the project were not aware of his condition, which contributed to difficulties in the recording process. "Nadie durante la grabación era consciente del estado de enfermedad terminal que tenía David Bowie, el único que lo sabía era Donnie Visconti porque era un gran amigo personal de David Bowie pero el resto no lo sabía." ← Music Radar Clan > David Bowie - BlackStar (lo que sabemos) | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=7gjhR5zK148&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**The "Real" Berlin Trilogy Theory** : A theory suggests that the true "Berlin Trilogy" might not solely consist of Bowie's three albums, but rather David Bowie's *Low*, Iggy Pop's *The Idiot*, and Brian Eno's *Music For Airports*. This perspective accounts for the intense collaborative spirit and the fact that many of Bowie's recordings were not exclusively made in Berlin. **The Greek Newspaper Ruse** : Bowie reportedly employed a clever trick to avoid recognition when leaving his apartment: he would carry a Greek newspaper under his arm. If someone suspected his identity, seeing the foreign paper would often lead them to dismiss the idea, thinking he was "just some Greek man." "Bowie had this thing when he left the building. He'd have a Greek newspaper under his arm, and when someone might say, hey, isn't that David Bowie? Then they'd see the newspaper and say, oh, well, I guess it can't be. It's just some Greek man on his way for us who's lucky." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hhii2_BVE7A ← david-bowie

**The Thin White Duke Persona - Thomas Jerome Newton Influence** : This amoral, hollow, damaged, and emotionless character, with his signature white shirt and waistcoat, emerged from an autobiography Bowie began while filming "The Man Who Fell to Earth," in which he played the doomed space alien Thomas Jerome Newton. Bowie loved the character and asked to keep the costuming, directly influencing his look for the next couple of years. "This character came from a sort of autobiography Bowie had begun while filming the man who fell to Earth, the movie where he played a doomed space alien named Thomas Jerome Newton." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2FyAZGUI_mk ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Theatrical Retirement of Ziggy Stardust** : Despite the overwhelming success of the Ziggy Stardust character, Bowie decided the persona had run its course and sought to retire it. He chose to do so in a highly theatrical manner, bowing out at the peak of his fame at a concert in one of London's most famous rock venues. "Bowie had decided that his Ziggy character had run its course and it was time to get out." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qC0Ee4-dpnI ← david-bowie
**Theatrical and Fashion Impact of Ziggy Stardust** : Bowie's Ziggy Stardust character revolutionized rock music through its theatricality, distinctive clothes, makeup, and overall presentation, blending hard rock with vaudeville, disposable pop with serious theater, and fashion with technology. Its "sexy and very sexual" nature was groundbreaking for its time, making cross-dressing and male makeup fashionable in the 1970s and inspiring millions to copy his haircut. "Bowie's character changed so much in terms of rock music. The theater, the clothes, the makeup, the presentation." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2RKchFW42Jc ← david-bowie

**Top of the Pops Performance (July 6, 1972)** : Bowie's seminal performance on Top of the Pops on July 6, 1972, with The Spiders from Mars, was highly influential. Dressed in a quilted jumpsuit, red boxing boots with green laces, and bright red-orange hair, Bowie's anisocoria (permanently dilated pupil from a childhood fight) added to his "otherworldly look." His public display of affection towards guitarist Mick Ronson (draping his arm around his shoulders) was considered "super duper gay" for the era and had a profound impact, leading to the immediate appearance of "Ziggy Clones" and helping young people feel accepted in their sexuality. "One especially interesting performance was on top of the pops on the BBC, July 6th, 1972." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

The mood at this show was described as "stunned," with plenty of denial evident among fans as the truth of his passing began to sink in. "I was at that Tuesday show in Toronto, and the word to describe the mood was stunned." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie

**Transition to "Blue-Eyed Plastic Soul"** : During the "Diamond Dogs" tour, Bowie began transitioning from his "spaceman" image to a more elegant, sophisticated look with shorter hair and tailored suits. This paralleled a shift in his musical interests towards American soul and R&B, leading to the smoother, funkier sound of "Young Americans." This endorsement of black music encouraged many of his fans to explore those genres. "Bowie became less space man and more elegant, shorter hair, tailored suits, an air of sophistication." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie

**Unrecorded Eccentricities (1974-1976)** : The period between 1974 and 1976 saw David Bowie engage in "hundreds" of eccentric and costly endeavors, frequently spending millions on what were considered "truly stupid things." Much of this information remains undocumented in his official biographies because Bowie himself, due to his mental state at the time, could not recall many of these activities or purchases. **Visconti and Moss Inspiration for "Heroes"** : Producer Tony Visconti provided a long-standing explanation for the lyrics of "Heroes," stating that David Bowie saw him embracing German singer Antonia Moss by the Berlin Wall. Visconti, from the West, and Moss, from the East, were depicted as hating the divided city but insisting on kissing by the wall as bullets flew from guard towers. Bowie later confirmed seeing the couple. "We've been told that one of the lovers is from the west, which is Visconti, and the other from the east, which is Moss." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DAjcCk9xYWk ← david-bowie
**Visionary Capabilities** : David Bowie was a documented visionary, accurately predicting the rise of phenomena such as digital music, social media, and gender fluidity. This aspect of his career is used by some to support the more outlandish claim that he could also have predicted the rise of Kanye West. "Now, it is true that Bowie was a documented visionary when it came to predicting the rise of things like digital music and social media and gender fluidity." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=pmKjZzypzvg ← david-bowie
**Visit to Iggy Pop** : Bowie was Iggy Pop's only visitor during his stay in a mental hospital, notably bringing him drugs. "By the way, his only visitor was David Bowie. He brought him drugs, but that's another story entirely." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wYuNolSDLFM ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Visited Iggy During Hospitalization** : David Bowie was one of only two visitors Iggy Pop received during his weeks-long detoxification and psychiatric evaluation at the UCLA Neuropsychiatric Hospital in October 1974. "He had two visitors. One was David Bowie and the other was Bowie's costume designer, a woman named Ola Hudson." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w-rihv544I8 ← david-bowie
**Vogue Magazine Inspiration for Ziggy's Hair** : After deciding on a new look, David and Angie Bowie searched fashion magazines, eventually finding a version of the desired "new hair thing" in a Vogue advertisement, which served as the blueprint for Ziggy's iconic style. "It was then that neither Bowie or Angie, nobody remembers who, found a version of this new hair thing in an ad in Vogue magazine." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Widespread Musical Appeal** : Bowie's music had such widespread appeal that it was played across diverse radio formats, including Top 40 stations and rock stations. It was considered "cool" in punk clubs, and his songs like "Fame" or "Young Americans" were often mixed in with dance music at disco venues, demonstrating his broad influence across genres. "And Bowie's cache had so much widespread appeal that his music was played on both top 40 stations and rock stations." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=P3xjW0A57Wk ← david-bowie
**Wish to Compose Exit Music (For a Film)** : David Bowie once confessed that *Exit Music (For a Film)* was the song he had always wished he could have composed himself. However, he also admitted that he felt he was not talented enough to have written such a piece. This remark stands as his most explicit acknowledgment of his admiration for Radiohead found in his interviews. "He referred to it on one occasion as the song he would have loved to have composed but wasn't good enough to have made." ← Music Radar Clan > Radiohead - Exit Music For a film tiene una historia un tanto curiosa | https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=1NgQgJwnoh8&list=PLBFijugu0fhAAIR-Ibh59aaU8VWg-SkLc
**Ziggy Stardust - Breakthrough and Theatricality** : The creation of Ziggy Stardust brought Bowie out of almost a decade of obscurity, elevating rock's theatricality to new levels. The character was presented as a "doomed spaceman with a Messiah concept," potentially involved in populating Earth with "Japanese style kabuki actors." Bowie used Ziggy to explore fashion, utilize his professional mime training from the 1960s, and experiment with art and sexuality. "this was the move that brought Bowie out of obscurity after almost a decade of dead ends." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust - Theatrical Rock Star Persona** : Bowie created Ziggy Stardust as a "doomed pansexual alien," using his acting and mime lessons to embody this character fully. This allowed him to sing, say, and do things he couldn't as "plain David Bowie." Ziggy's impact on rock in 1972 was immense, challenging the prevailing jeans and T-shirts aesthetic with makeup, costumes, and theatrical concerts featuring choreography, transforming rock into a full, immersive experience. "This idea of coming up with a pre-packaged synthetic ultra glamorous, ultra theatrical rock star." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sPCrATqBdeA ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Alter-Ego** : Ziggy Stardust was one of David Bowie's first and most enduring alter-egos and stage characters, described as a "bisexual alien dressed up all in glitter." This persona was immensely popular in England in late 1972 and early 1973, with the whole country talking about him. "Ziggy Stardust, one of Bowie's first and most enduring of all his alter-egos and stage characters, had been the ticket." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=huAvyInzz3Q ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Character's Impact** : Bowie's Ziggy Stardust character offered significant hope to many, presenting himself as a weirdly androgynous, potentially bisexual figure who wore makeup and glitter and performed provocative acts on stage, such as simulating oral sex with his guitarist, Mick Ronson. Despite Bowie himself not being 100% gay, the character's persona profoundly impacted and inspired closeted people worldwide. "Ziggy was this weirdly androgynous, maybe bisexual creature who wore makeup and glitter and did all kinds of looed things on stage, like simulating oral sex in his guitarist, Mick Ronson." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hswtuenFwvM ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Costume Inspiration** : Ziggy Stardust's costumes drew inspiration from the main characters of Stanley Kubrick's controversial film *A Clockwork Orange*, which was banned in the UK for its depictions of violence and sex, as well as from Japanese designer Yasuko Hayashi. "Ziggy's clothes were inspired in equal parts by what we saw with the main characters in the film, a clockwork orange... And a Japanese designer named Yasuko Hayashi." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Debut (February 1972)** : David Bowie formally debuted the Ziggy Stardust character on February 10, 1972, at the Torquay Jug Pub in London. At the time, he was still a minor pop star, resulting in low attendance, but this performance marked the beginning of Ziggy's ascent. "Then on February 10th, 1972, David Bowie debuted the Ziggy character at the Torey Jug Pub in London." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Hairdo Creation** : Bowie's iconic "Ziggy Stardust puff ball" hairstyle, a striking mullet, was conceived from photos in a fashion magazine called Honey (for the front) and French Vogue (for the back and sides). His mother's stylist, Susie Fussy, from Evelyn Page salon, helped create it, dyeing it "Schwartzkoft red" and stiffening it with an anti-dandruff treatment called Guard. This unisex haircut became a defining style of the era. "They created the famous Ziggy Stardust puff ball." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Inspiration** : David Bowie's iconic Ziggy Stardust character was partly inspired by the American singer Vince Taylor, known for his 1959 song "Brand New Cadillac." "The original was by Vince Taylor, an American singer who provided part of the inspiration for David Bowie's Ziggy Stardust character." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=_KJ60im4KAc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Persona** : Introduced in 1972, Ziggy Stardust became Bowie's most famous character, transforming the course of rock music. Ziggy was a doomed, drug-addled, glam spaceman, drawing inspiration from figures like Andy Warhol, Lou Reed, Bob Dylan, Frank Sinatra, and an obscure American singer named Vince Taylor. The character was described as part *Clockwork Orange* and part autobiography. Ziggy, performing with his band The Spiders From Mars, existed for only two years but became an enduring rock and roll icon, subject to books, PhD dissertations, and debates by scholars. Bowie's unique use of image and theater made Ziggy one of the most profound inventions in rock history, inspiring British kids bored with mainstream rock to create punk rock. "Bowie called his creation Ziggy Star Dust." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0xd0Hf5REg4 ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust Tour Theatricality** : The tour supporting "The Rise and Fall of Ziggy Stardust and The Spiders from Mars" (January 29, 1972 - July 3, 1973) set a new standard for theatricality in rock, incorporating "big end themic songs, costume changes, choreography, makeup, tall boots, and ridiculously high platform shoes" along with "daring sexual ambiguity." "the tour, which ran from January 29th, 1972 to July 3rd, 1973, was the most theatrical thing that rock had ever seen to that point." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=blDNqVFheAw ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust and Mullet Popularization** : David Bowie's debut of the Ziggy Stardust character gave a jump start to the mullet hairstyle in the late 1960s. The mullet, having been largely invisible, was then seen as a radical, scary, and shocking look, contributing to its spread across society. "When David Bowie's debut of the Ziggy Stardust character gave it a jump start, the mullet was seen as radical and scary and shocking." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bferkEWvJg0 ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust's Cultural Impact** : Through his "weirdly androgynous Ziggy Stardust character," David Bowie became one of the most influential alternative artists of all time. Ziggy Stardust shattered the myth of the "hetero-metro rock star with the guitar," proving that a performer could be sexually ambiguous and still achieve significant commercial success. ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z9T9wi0vEvc ← david-bowie
**Ziggy Stardust's Orange Puffball Haircut** : Around eight years after his early advocacy, Bowie, heavily influenced by his wife Angie, debuted the iconic orange puffball with a tail haircut, which became central to his Ziggy Stardust persona and is regarded as one of rock's most influential hairstyles. "The orange puffball with a tail, sported by Bowie and his Ziggy Stardust face." ← https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Q3zkJX8S4Xc ← david-bowie ← david-bowie
